## ğŸ“– PART B: EXPLANATION (30%) - Deep Theory

### B.1 ALIGNMENT FUNDAMENTALS

#### B.1.1 What is Sequence Alignment?
```
DEFINITION:
â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•
Sequence Alignment = Arranging sequences to identify 
regions of similarity that may indicate:
â”œâ”€â”€ Functional relationship
â”œâ”€â”€ Structural relationship
â””â”€â”€ Evolutionary relationship

EXAMPLE:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Sequence 1: ATGCGATCGATCG
Sequence 2: ATGC-ATCGTTCG
                 â†‘     â†‘
                gap  mismatch

Alignment shows:
â”œâ”€â”€ Matches: Most positions identical
â”œâ”€â”€ Gaps: Insertions or deletions (indels)
â””â”€â”€ Mismatches: Point mutations

WHY ALIGNMENT REVEALS FUNCTION:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
AXIOM: Similar sequences â†’ Similar structure â†’ Similar function

If protein A (known function) aligns well with protein B (unknown):
â†’ B likely has similar function to A

This is the basis of:
â”œâ”€â”€ Gene annotation
â”œâ”€â”€ Function prediction
â”œâ”€â”€ Drug target identification
â””â”€â”€ Understanding disease mutations
```

#### B.1.2 Global vs Local Alignment
```
GLOBAL ALIGNMENT (Needleman-Wunsch):
â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•
â€¢ Aligns ENTIRE length of both sequences
â€¢ Penalizes all gaps
â€¢ Best for: Similar-length, related sequences

EXAMPLE USE CASE:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Compare human TERT vs mouse TERT (both ~1130 amino acids)
â†’ Global alignment appropriate
â†’ Want to see all conserved/divergent regions

    Human TERT:  MSRARTYTQLR...entire protein...KEALRY
    Mouse TERT:  MSRARSYTQLR...entire protein...KEALRY
                      â†‘
                 Single AA difference

â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

LOCAL ALIGNMENT (Smith-Waterman):
â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•
â€¢ Finds BEST matching region
â€¢ Ignores poor matches outside
â€¢ Best for: Finding domains, partial matches

EXAMPLE USE CASE:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Find TERT domain in a long chromosomal sequence
â†’ Local alignment appropriate
â†’ Only care about the domain region

    Chromosome:  .....NNNNN[TERT DOMAIN]NNNNN.....
    TERT query:              [TERT DOMAIN]
                             â†‘
                      Only this part aligns

COMPARISON:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
â”Œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¬â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¬â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”
â”‚    Feature      â”‚     Global      â”‚     Local       â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¼â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¼â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¤
â”‚ Sequences       â”‚ Similar length  â”‚ Any length      â”‚
â”‚ Coverage        â”‚ Entire sequence â”‚ Best region     â”‚
â”‚ Gaps at ends    â”‚ Penalized       â”‚ Not penalized   â”‚
â”‚ Use case        â”‚ Compare genes   â”‚ Find domains    â”‚
â”‚ Algorithm       â”‚ Needleman-Wunschâ”‚ Smith-Waterman  â”‚
â””â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”´â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”´â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”˜
```

### B.2 SCORING SYSTEMS

#### B.2.1 Match, Mismatch, and Gap Scores
```
SCORING PHILOSOPHY:
â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•
Goal: Quantify how "good" an alignment is
Higher score = Better alignment

SIMPLE SCORING (DNA):
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Match:    +1 (reward similarity)
Mismatch: -1 (penalize difference)
Gap:      -2 (penalize insertion/deletion)

EXAMPLE:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Seq1: ATGC-A
Seq2: ATGCTA
      â†‘â†‘â†‘â†‘â†‘â†‘
      MMMMGM (M=match, G=gap)

Score = 4Ã—(+1) + 1Ã—(-2) + 1Ã—(+1) = +3

AFFINE GAP PENALTY:
â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•
Problem with linear: Each gap position costs same
Reality: One gap event is more likely than many

Solution: Affine penalty
â”œâ”€â”€ Gap open: -10 (first position of gap)
â””â”€â”€ Gap extend: -1 (each additional position)

EXAMPLE:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Linear (gap = -2):
Seq1: ATG---CTA
Score: 3Ã—M + 3Ã—G = 3Ã—(+1) + 3Ã—(-2) = -3

Affine (open = -10, extend = -1):
Seq1: ATG---CTA
Score: 3Ã—M + Open + 2Ã—Extend = 3 - 10 - 2 = -9

But for multiple small gaps:
Seq1: A-TG-C-A
Linear: 3Ã—(-2) = -6
Affine: 3Ã—(-10) = -30 â† Heavily penalizes!

â†’ Affine prefers one long gap over multiple short gaps
â†’ Biologically more realistic
```

#### B.2.2 Substitution Matrices (BLOSUM, PAM)
```
SUBSTITUTION MATRICES FOR PROTEINS:
â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•
Problem: For proteins, "match" isn't just identical
Some substitutions are common (Leuâ†”Ile), others rare (Trpâ†”Gly)

Solution: Use matrices that encode evolutionary substitution frequency

BLOSUM (BLOcks SUbstitution Matrix):
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
How it was created:
1. Collect conserved protein blocks
2. Count how often each AA substitutes for each
3. Log-odds score: observed/expected ratio

BLOSUM62 excerpt:
       A   R   N   D   C   Q   E   G   H   I
   A   4  -1  -2  -2   0  -1  -1   0  -2  -1
   R  -1   5   0  -2  -3   1   0  -2   0  -3
   N  -2   0   6   1  -3   0   0   0   1  -3
   D  -2  -2   1   6  -3   0   2  -1  -1  -3
   C   0  -3  -3  -3   9  -3  -4  -3  -3  -1
   ...

Reading: Aâ†’A = +4 (good), Aâ†’R = -1 (poor), Câ†’C = +9 (cysteine rare!)

BLOSUM NUMBER MEANING:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
BLOSUM80: Blocks with â‰¥80% identity
          â†’ Very similar sequences
          â†’ Stringent matching

BLOSUM62: Blocks with â‰¥62% identity
          â†’ General purpose (default)
          â†’ Most commonly used

BLOSUM45: Blocks with â‰¥45% identity
          â†’ Distant relationships
          â†’ More tolerant of substitutions

PAM (Point Accepted Mutation):
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Based on evolutionary model of accepted mutations

PAM1: 1% amino acids mutated
PAM250: ~80% mutated (extrapolated)

Higher PAM = More divergent sequences

WHEN TO USE WHICH:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
â”Œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¬â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”
â”‚ Sequence similarity â”‚ Matrix to use                   â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¼â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¤
â”‚ Very similar (>80%) â”‚ BLOSUM80, PAM40                 â”‚
â”‚ Moderate (60-80%)   â”‚ BLOSUM62 (default)              â”‚
â”‚ Distant (<30%)      â”‚ BLOSUM45, PAM250                â”‚
â””â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”´â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”˜
```

### B.3 ALIGNMENT ALGORITHMS

#### B.3.1 Needleman-Wunsch (Global Alignment)
```
ALGORITHM OVERVIEW:
â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•
Dynamic programming algorithm for global alignment
Time: O(n Ã— m), Space: O(n Ã— m)

STEP 1: INITIALIZATION
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Create matrix of size (m+1) Ã— (n+1)
Fill first row and column with gap penalties

Example: Seq1 = "CAT", Seq2 = "CT", gap = -2

        -    C    T
    â”Œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¬â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¬â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”
  - â”‚  0  â”‚ -2  â”‚ -4  â”‚
    â”œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¼â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¼â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¤
  C â”‚ -2  â”‚  ?  â”‚  ?  â”‚
    â”œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¼â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¼â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¤
  A â”‚ -4  â”‚  ?  â”‚  ?  â”‚
    â”œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¼â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¼â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¤
  T â”‚ -6  â”‚  ?  â”‚  ?  â”‚
    â””â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”´â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”´â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”˜

STEP 2: MATRIX FILLING
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
For each cell (i,j), compute:

F(i,j) = max of:
â”œâ”€â”€ F(i-1,j-1) + score(seq1[i], seq2[j])  â† diagonal (match/mismatch)
â”œâ”€â”€ F(i-1,j) + gap                         â† up (gap in seq2)
â””â”€â”€ F(i,j-1) + gap                         â† left (gap in seq1)

Filled matrix:
        -    C    T
    â”Œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¬â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¬â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”
  - â”‚  0  â”‚ -2  â”‚ -4  â”‚
    â”œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¼â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¼â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¤
  C â”‚ -2  â”‚ +1  â”‚ -1  â”‚  â† C-C match = +1
    â”œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¼â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¼â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¤
  A â”‚ -4  â”‚ -1  â”‚  0  â”‚
    â”œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¼â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¼â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¤
  T â”‚ -6  â”‚ -3  â”‚ +1  â”‚  â† T-T match = +1
    â””â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”´â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”´â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”˜

STEP 3: TRACEBACK
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Start from bottom-right (final score = +1)
Follow path that gave maximum at each step

Path: (3,2) â†’ (2,1) â†’ (1,1) â†’ (0,0)

Alignment:
CAT
C-T
Score: +1
```

#### B.3.2 Smith-Waterman (Local Alignment)
```
KEY DIFFERENCES FROM GLOBAL:
â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

1ï¸âƒ£ INITIALIZATION
   Global: First row/column = cumulative gap penalties
   Local:  First row/column = 0

2ï¸âƒ£ RECURRENCE
   Global: F(i,j) = max(diagonal, up, left)
   Local:  F(i,j) = max(diagonal, up, left, 0) â† ADD ZERO!

3ï¸âƒ£ TRACEBACK START
   Global: Start from bottom-right corner
   Local:  Start from maximum value anywhere in matrix

4ï¸âƒ£ TRACEBACK END
   Global: Continue to top-left corner
   Local:  Stop when cell value is 0

EXAMPLE:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Seq1: ACGTCG (longer)
Seq2: GTC (shorter, looking for this pattern)

Local alignment matrix would find:
   ...GTC...
      GTC
      â†‘â†‘â†‘
   Perfect match region (local)

The flanking parts (AC... and ...G) are ignored
â†’ No penalty for end gaps
â†’ Only the best part matters
```

### B.4 BLAST - PRACTICAL SEQUENCE SEARCH

#### B.4.1 How BLAST Works
```
BLAST = Basic Local Alignment Search Tool
â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

WHY NOT USE SMITH-WATERMAN DIRECTLY?
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Problem: SW is O(n Ã— m)
Database has billions of sequences
â†’ Would take forever!

BLAST Solution: Heuristic approach
â†’ Fast but might miss some weak matches
â†’ Trade exactness for speed

BLAST ALGORITHM:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

Step 1: SEEDING (Word matching)
â”œâ”€â”€ Break query into "words" (k-mers)
â”œâ”€â”€ For protein: 3-mers (default)
â”œâ”€â”€ For DNA: 11-mers (default)
â””â”€â”€ Find all positions in database with words

Example:
Query: MASHTSN...
Words: MAS, ASH, SHT, HTS, TSN...
Database match: Found SHT at position 4521!

Step 2: EXTENSION
â”œâ”€â”€ From each seed match, extend in both directions
â”œâ”€â”€ Use ungapped alignment first
â”œâ”€â”€ If score above threshold, do gapped extension
â””â”€â”€ Report significant alignments

Step 3: EVALUATION
â”œâ”€â”€ Calculate E-value for each hit
â”œâ”€â”€ E-value = Expected number of hits by chance
â”œâ”€â”€ Lower E-value = More significant
â””â”€â”€ Typically report E < 0.01 or E < 1e-5
```

#### B.4.2 Interpreting BLAST Results
```
BLAST OUTPUT EXPLAINED:
â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

E-VALUE:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
E = Expected hits in database of same size by random chance

E-value interpretation:
â”œâ”€â”€ E = 0:     Perfect match (theoretically impossible)
â”œâ”€â”€ E = 1e-50: Extremely significant (essentially identical)
â”œâ”€â”€ E = 1e-10: Highly significant (clearly homologous)
â”œâ”€â”€ E = 0.01:  Significant (likely related)
â”œâ”€â”€ E = 1:     Borderline (might be real or chance)
â”œâ”€â”€ E = 10:    Not significant (probably random)
â””â”€â”€ E = 100:   Definitely random

BIT SCORE:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Normalized alignment score
Higher = Better
Independent of database size (unlike E-value)

PERCENT IDENTITY:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
% of aligned positions that are identical

Identity guidelines:
â”œâ”€â”€ >70%: Very close homologs (same function likely)
â”œâ”€â”€ 40-70%: Clear homologs (similar function)
â”œâ”€â”€ 25-40%: Distant homologs (conserved domain/fold)
â””â”€â”€ <25%: Twilight zone (homology uncertain)

QUERY COVERAGE:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
% of query sequence that aligned

Coverage interpretation:
â”œâ”€â”€ 100%: Full-length match (gene-level homolog)
â”œâ”€â”€ 50-80%: Partial match (shared domain)
â”œâ”€â”€ <30%: Small region match (motif/short domain)
```

---

## ğŸ”¬ PART C: USES & APPLICATIONS (30%)

### C.1 USES IN BIOINFORMATICS

#### C.1.1 Gene Function Prediction
```
THE HOMOLOGY INFERENCE WORKFLOW:
â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

1ï¸âƒ£ FIND HOMOLOGS
   â”œâ”€â”€ Take unknown gene sequence
   â”œâ”€â”€ BLAST against nr/SwissProt database
   â”œâ”€â”€ Collect significant hits (E < 0.01)
   â””â”€â”€ Sort by E-value

2ï¸âƒ£ ANALYZE TOP HITS
   â”œâ”€â”€ Check if annotated with function
   â”œâ”€â”€ Look for consistent function among hits
   â””â”€â”€ Note which organisms have homologs

3ï¸âƒ£ INFER FUNCTION
   â”œâ”€â”€ If multiple hits have same function â†’ Likely!
   â”œâ”€â”€ If conserved across distant species â†’ Important!
   â””â”€â”€ Document predicted function with confidence

EXAMPLE:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Unknown gene from new organism
â†“
BLAST search
â†“
Top hit: Human TERT (E = 1e-100)
Other hits: Mouse TERT, Zebrafish TERT...
â†“
Conclusion: This is a telomerase gene!

CAUTION:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
â€¢ Transfer function only for orthologs (same function likely)
â€¢ Paralogs may have diverged function
â€¢ Low homology = low confidence prediction
```

#### C.1.2 Evolutionary Analysis
```
BUILDING PHYLOGENETIC TREES:
â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

WORKFLOW:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
1. Collect homologous sequences from multiple species
2. Multiple sequence alignment (MSA)
3. Calculate evolutionary distances
4. Build phylogenetic tree
5. Infer evolutionary relationships

ALIGNMENT IS CRITICAL:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Poor alignment â†’ Wrong tree!

Each column in MSA represents:
â”œâ”€â”€ Homologous position
â”œâ”€â”€ Descended from common ancestor
â””â”€â”€ Comparable for evolutionary analysis

EXAMPLE WITH AGING GENES:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
SIRT1 from: Human, Mouse, Fish, Worm, Yeast

MSA reveals:
â”œâ”€â”€ Core deacetylase domain: Highly conserved
â”œâ”€â”€ Regulatory regions: Species-specific
â””â”€â”€ NAD+ binding site: Absolutely conserved

Tree shows:
â”œâ”€â”€ Human/Mouse cluster together (mammals)
â”œâ”€â”€ Fish more distant (vertebrates)
â”œâ”€â”€ Worm even more (metazoa)
â””â”€â”€ Yeast most distant (eukaryotes)

IMMORTALITY INSIGHT:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Conservation from yeast to human = 
Essential for life = 
Important aging pathway target!
```

### C.2 USES IN GENETIC ENGINEERING

#### C.2.1 CRISPR Off-Target Prediction
```
OFF-TARGET = CRISPR cutting the wrong place!
â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

WHY ALIGNMENT MATTERS:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
gRNA (20 bp) might match other genome sites with mismatches
â†’ Could cause unintended edits
â†’ Safety concern for therapy

WORKFLOW:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

Step 1: DESIGN gRNA
        Target: 5'-ATGCGATCGATCGATCGATCNGG-3'
                   â†‘â”€â”€â”€ 20 bp gRNA â”€â”€â†‘ PAM

Step 2: SEARCH GENOME FOR SIMILAR SITES
        â””â”€â”€ Use alignment (BLASTN or specialized tools)

Step 3: ANALYZE POTENTIAL OFF-TARGETS
        â”œâ”€â”€ How many mismatches?
        â”œâ”€â”€ Where are mismatches? (seed region = worse)
        â””â”€â”€ Is it in a gene? (worse if yes)

Step 4: CHOOSE gRNA WITH FEWEST OFF-TARGETS

TOOLS USING ALIGNMENT:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
â”œâ”€â”€ Cas-OFFinder (exact pattern matching)
â”œâ”€â”€ CRISPOR (scores off-targets)
â”œâ”€â”€ Benchling (commercial, user-friendly)
â””â”€â”€ All use sequence alignment internally!

EXAMPLE:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
gRNA:   ATGCGATCGATCGATCGATC
        ||||||||||||||| ||||
Site:   ATGCGATCGATCGATGGATC (1 mismatch)
                        â†‘
        This could be an off-target!

Module 3 knowledge enables:
â”œâ”€â”€ Understanding alignment scores
â”œâ”€â”€ Interpreting off-target predictions
â””â”€â”€ Making informed gRNA choices
```

#### C.2.2 Protein Engineering
```
DESIGNING IMPROVED PROTEINS:
â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

ALIGNMENT IDENTIFIES:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
1. Conserved residues (don't change these!)
2. Variable positions (can modify these)
3. Functional domains (critical regions)

WORKFLOW:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

Step 1: MSA of protein family
        (e.g., all known telomerases)

Step 2: Identify conserved residues
        * = absolutely conserved (essential)
        : = strongly conserved (important)
        . = weakly conserved (possibly important)
        (blank) = variable (can modify)

Step 3: Design mutations
        â”œâ”€â”€ Keep conserved positions
        â”œâ”€â”€ Modify variable positions for desired property
        â””â”€â”€ Test experimentally

EXAMPLE - IMPROVING TELOMERASE:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Goal: Make hyperactive telomerase for life extension

MSA of TERT from many species reveals:
â”œâ”€â”€ Active site residues: ABSOLUTELY conserved
â”‚   â†’ Don't touch these!
â”œâ”€â”€ RNA-binding domain: Highly conserved
â”‚   â†’ Critical for function
â””â”€â”€ Regulatory region: Variable
    â†’ Can modify for higher activity!

Strategy:
â”œâ”€â”€ Mutation in regulatory region
â”œâ”€â”€ Remove autoinhibition
â””â”€â”€ Higher telomere extension activity

This is how Sinclair lab improved genes for age reversal!
```

### C.3 USES IN IMMORTALITY RESEARCH

#### C.3.1 Finding Longevity Genes
```
COMPARATIVE GENOMICS FOR LONGEVITY:
â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

KEY QUESTION:
Why do some animals live much longer than others?
â”œâ”€â”€ Bowhead whale: 200+ years
â”œâ”€â”€ Naked mole rat: 30+ years (vs 3 years for mouse)
â”œâ”€â”€ Greenland shark: 400+ years
â””â”€â”€ Human: 80-120 years

ALIGNMENT-BASED APPROACH:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

Step 1: Compare genomes of long-lived vs short-lived
Step 2: Find sequences unique to long-lived
Step 3: Identify conserved differences
Step 4: Test candidates for longevity function

DISCOVERIES MADE THIS WAY:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

1ï¸âƒ£ NAKED MOLE RAT
   â”œâ”€â”€ Aligned cancer-related genes with mouse
   â”œâ”€â”€ Found unique INK4 gene arrangement
   â”œâ”€â”€ p16 and p19 expressed differently
   â””â”€â”€ Explains cancer resistance!

2ï¸âƒ£ BOWHEAD WHALE
   â”œâ”€â”€ Compared to other cetaceans
   â”œâ”€â”€ Found ERCC1 and HDAC3 variants
   â”œâ”€â”€ Enhanced DNA repair genes
   â””â”€â”€ Better genome maintenance

3ï¸âƒ£ ACROSS MANY SPECIES
   â”œâ”€â”€ Long-lived animals have:
   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ More DNA repair gene copies
   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Enhanced p53 pathway
   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Better telomere maintenance
   â””â”€â”€ All found through alignment!
```

#### C.3.2 Epigenetic Clock Conservation
```
EPIGENETIC CLOCKS ACROSS SPECIES:
â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

DISCOVERY (2023):
Universal mammalian aging clock based on conserved CpG sites!

HOW ALIGNMENT WAS USED:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

Step 1: Identify clock CpG sites in human genome
       (353 sites from Horvath clock)

Step 2: Align human genome to other mammals
       (mouse, dog, cat, elephant, whale, etc.)

Step 3: Find conserved CpGs across species
       (~200 sites conserved in all mammals)

Step 4: Build universal age predictor
       Works for any mammal!

IMPLICATIONS:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
â”œâ”€â”€ Aging is deeply conserved (evolution)
â”œâ”€â”€ Same interventions might work across species
â”œâ”€â”€ Can test anti-aging drugs in mice, translate to humans
â””â”€â”€ Alignment enabled this breakthrough!

PRACTICAL APPLICATION:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
When testing age reversal interventions:
â”œâ”€â”€ Use conserved clock sites
â”œâ”€â”€ Test in model organisms
â”œâ”€â”€ Predict human translation
â””â”€â”€ All requires alignment knowledge!
```

â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Test: from Bio import Seq
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Learn: Creating Seq objects
â”‚   â”‚   ```python
â”‚   â”‚   from Bio.Seq import Seq
â”‚   â”‚   dna = Seq("ATGCGATCGATCG")
â”‚   â”‚   print(dna)  # ATGCGATCGATCG
â”‚   â”‚   print(len(dna))  # 13
â”‚   â”‚   ```
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Practice: Basic string operations
â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€ Afternoon (2 hours)
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Study: Seq methods
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ .complement()
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ .reverse_complement()
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ .transcribe()
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ .translate()
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Slicing [start:end]
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Code examples:
â”‚       ```python
â”‚       dna = Seq("ATGCGATCGATCG")
â”‚       print(dna.complement())  # TACGCTAGCTAGC
â”‚       print(dna.reverse_complement())  # CGATCGATCGCAT
â”‚       print(dna.transcribe())  # AUGCGAUCGAUCG
â”‚       print(dna[:6].translate())  # MR
â”‚       ```
â”‚
â””â”€â”€ Evening (1 hour)
    â”œâ”€â”€ Practice: Solve Rosalind problems with Biopython
    â”œâ”€â”€ Compare: Manual code vs Biopython
    â””â”€â”€ Note: Biopython handles edge cases!

### A.3 WEEK 3: File Formats & Automation (Days 15-21)
```
ğŸ“… Day 15-16: Sequence File Formats
â”œâ”€â”€ Morning (2 hours)
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Study: FASTA format in detail
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ >header line (ID, description)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Sequence on following lines
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Simple, universal
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ No quality or annotations
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Study: FASTQ format
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ @header (sequence ID)
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Sequence
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ +header (optional)
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Quality scores (ASCII)
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Used for raw sequencing data
â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€ Afternoon (2 hours)
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Study: GenBank format
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Rich annotations
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ LOCUS, DEFINITION, ACCESSION
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ FEATURES section (CDS, gene, etc.)
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ ORIGIN (sequence)
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Practice: Parse GenBank files
â”‚       ```python
â”‚       for record in SeqIO.parse("gene.gb", "genbank"):
â”‚           for feature in record.features:
â”‚               if feature.type == "CDS":
â”‚                   print(feature.qualifiers)
â”‚       ```

## ğŸ“– PART B: EXPLANATION (30%) - Deep Theory

### B.1 BIOPYTHON CORE

#### B.1.1 The Seq Object
```
WHY BIOPYTHON?
â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•
Standard Python strings work for sequences, but:
â”œâ”€â”€ No biological awareness
â”œâ”€â”€ Don't know about complement, transcription, translation
â”œâ”€â”€ No validation (could have invalid characters)
â””â”€â”€ No integration with databases

Biopython Seq object:
â”œâ”€â”€ Biologically aware
â”œâ”€â”€ Has biological methods built-in
â”œâ”€â”€ Validates sequences
â””â”€â”€ Integrates with rest of Biopython

SEQ OBJECT METHODS:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

COMPLEMENT:
    A â†’ T, T â†’ A, G â†’ C, C â†’ G
    
    dna = Seq("ATGCGATCGATCG")
    dna.complement()  # TACGCTAGCTAGC

REVERSE COMPLEMENT:
    Complement + Reverse
    This is what you get on opposite strand!
    
    dna = Seq("ATGCGATCGATCG")
    dna.reverse_complement()  # CGATCGATCGCAT
    
    Think: If forward is 5'-ATG-3'
           Then reverse is 3'-TAC-5' (read as 5'-CAT-3')

TRANSCRIBE:
    DNA â†’ RNA (T â†’ U)
    
    dna = Seq("ATGCGATCGATCG")
    dna.transcribe()  # AUGCGAUCGAUCG

TRANSLATE:
    RNA/DNA â†’ Protein (using genetic code)
    
    dna = Seq("ATGAAAGCTTAG")
    dna.translate()  # MKA* (M=Met, K=Lys, A=Ala, *=Stop)

INTERNAL REPRESENTATION:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Seq objects are immutable (like Python strings)
Can convert to mutable: MutableSeq

from Bio.Seq import MutableSeq
mseq = MutableSeq("ATGC")
mseq[0] = "C"  # Now "CTGC" - allowed!
```

#### B.1.2 SeqRecord - Sequences with Context
```
SEQRECORD = SEQ + METADATA:
â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

SeqRecord contains:
â”œâ”€â”€ seq: The Seq object
â”œâ”€â”€ id: Short identifier (accession)
â”œâ”€â”€ name: Name (gene name, etc.)
â”œâ”€â”€ description: Full description
â”œâ”€â”€ annotations: Dictionary of annotations
â”œâ”€â”€ features: List of SeqFeature objects
â”œâ”€â”€ dbxrefs: Database cross-references
â””â”€â”€ letter_annotations: Per-letter annotations

EXAMPLE:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
from Bio.SeqRecord import SeqRecord
from Bio.Seq import Seq

record = SeqRecord(
    Seq("ATGAAAGCTTAG"),
    id="TERT_001",
    name="TERT",
    description="Human telomerase reverse transcriptase",
    annotations={"organism": "Homo sapiens", "date": "2024-01-15"}
)

print(record.id)          # TERT_001
print(record.seq)         # ATGAAAGCTTAG
print(record.description) # Human telomerase...

FEATURES (for GenBank records):
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Features describe parts of the sequence:
â”œâ”€â”€ gene: Gene location
â”œâ”€â”€ CDS: Coding sequence (what gets translated)
â”œâ”€â”€ exon: Exon locations
â”œâ”€â”€ intron: Intron locations
â””â”€â”€ misc_feature: Other features

Accessing features:
for feature in record.features:
    if feature.type == "CDS":
        location = feature.location  # Start/end positions
        product = feature.qualifiers.get("product", [""])[0]
        print(f"CDS: {location}, Product: {product}")
```

### B.2 NCBI ENTREZ SYSTEM

#### B.2.1 How Entrez Works
```
ENTREZ = NCBI'S DATABASE SEARCH SYSTEM:
â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

ARCHITECTURE:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
                    â”Œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”
    Your Script     â”‚    Entrez       â”‚    NCBI Servers
        â”‚           â”‚                 â”‚         â”‚
        â”‚ esearch â”€â”€â–ºâ”‚  Search Query â”€â”€â–ºâ”‚â”€â”€â”€â–º     â”‚
        â”‚â—„â”€â”€ IDs â”€â”€â”€â”€â”‚â—„â”€â”€ ID List â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”‚â—„â”€â”€â”€     â”‚
        â”‚           â”‚                 â”‚         â”‚
        â”‚ efetch â”€â”€â”€â–ºâ”‚  Fetch by ID â”€â”€â–ºâ”‚â”€â”€â”€â–º     â”‚
        â”‚â—„â”€â”€ Data â”€â”€â”€â”‚â—„â”€â”€ Full Data â”€â”€â”€â”‚â—„â”€â”€â”€     â”‚
                    â””â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”˜

KEY FUNCTIONS:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

1ï¸âƒ£ ESEARCH - Find IDs matching query
   Entrez.esearch(db="nucleotide", term="TERT human")
   â†’ Returns: List of matching IDs

2ï¸âƒ£ EFETCH - Download by ID
   Entrez.efetch(db="nucleotide", id="NM_198253", rettype="fasta")
   â†’ Returns: Full sequence record

3ï¸âƒ£ EINFO - Get database information
   Entrez.einfo(db="nucleotide")
   â†’ Returns: Database statistics, fields

4ï¸âƒ£ ELINK - Find related records
   Entrez.elink(dbfrom="gene", db="protein", id="7015")
   â†’ Returns: Related protein IDs

IMPORTANT RULES:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
â€¢ MUST set Entrez.email (identifies you to NCBI)
â€¢ Rate limit: 3 requests/second (10 with API key)
â€¢ Get API key: ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/account/settings
â€¢ Always close handles!
â€¢ Be respectful of NCBI resources
```

#### B.2.2 Search Query Syntax
```
ENTREZ SEARCH QUERY LANGUAGE:
â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

BASIC SYNTAX:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
term[field]

Examples:
â”œâ”€â”€ TERT[Gene]           # Search gene name
â”œâ”€â”€ human[Organism]      # Search organism
â”œâ”€â”€ 2024[PDAT]           # Publication date
â””â”€â”€ mRNA[Filter]         # Filter by molecule type

COMBINING SEARCHES:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
AND: Both terms required
     "TERT[Gene] AND human[Organism]"

OR:  Either term
     "TERT[Gene] OR hTERT[Gene]"

NOT: Exclude term
     "kinase[Gene] NOT cancer[Title]"

USEFUL FIELD CODES:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
[Gene]      - Gene symbol/name
[Organism]  - Species
[All]       - All fields
[Title]     - Title only
[Author]    - Author name
[PDAT]      - Publication date
[Filter]    - Apply filters (mRNA, protein, etc.)
[ACCN]      - Accession number

EXAMPLE COMPLEX QUERY:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
# Find human aging-related genes from last 5 years
query = "(aging[Title] OR longevity[Title]) AND human[Organism] AND 2020:2024[PDAT]"

handle = Entrez.esearch(
    db="gene",
    term=query,
    retmax=100  # Maximum results
)
```

### B.3 DATABASE ECOSYSTEM

#### B.3.1 Choosing the Right Database
```
DATABASE SELECTION GUIDE:
â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

WHAT DO YOU NEED?      â†’     USE THIS DATABASE
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

DNA/RNA sequences      â†’     NCBI GenBank/RefSeq
                             â€¢ GenBank: Everything submitted
                             â€¢ RefSeq: Curated, standardized

Protein sequences      â†’     UniProt or NCBI Protein
                             â€¢ UniProt: Best annotations
                             â€¢ NCBI: Good for cross-reference

Gene information       â†’     NCBI Gene or Ensembl
                             â€¢ NCBI Gene: Gene summaries, links
                             â€¢ Ensembl: Genome context

Literature             â†’     PubMed
                             â€¢ Comprehensive biomedical lit
                             â€¢ Links to sequences

Expression data        â†’     GEO or GTEx
                             â€¢ GEO: Raw datasets
                             â€¢ GTEx: Tissue expression atlas

Variants               â†’     ClinVar, gnomAD, dbSNP
                             â€¢ ClinVar: Clinical significance
                             â€¢ gnomAD: Population frequencies
                             â€¢ dbSNP: All variants

Aging research         â†’     HAGR databases
                             â€¢ GenAge: Aging genes
                             â€¢ LongevityMap: Longevity variants
                             â€¢ AnAge: Species lifespan data

DATABASE IDENTIFIERS:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Each database has unique ID formats:

â€¢ NCBI Gene ID: numeric (e.g., 7015 for TERT)
â€¢ RefSeq mRNA: NM_XXXXXX (e.g., NM_198253)
â€¢ RefSeq protein: NP_XXXXXX (e.g., NP_937983)
â€¢ UniProt: P12345 or Q6FH01
â€¢ Ensembl gene: ENSG00000000001
â€¢ Ensembl transcript: ENST00000000001
```

## ğŸ”¬ PART C: USES & APPLICATIONS (30%)

### C.1 USES IN BIOINFORMATICS

#### C.1.1 Batch Sequence Analysis
```
AUTOMATING SEQUENCE ANALYSIS:
â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

WORKFLOW EXAMPLE - ANALYZE GENE FAMILY:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

Goal: Analyze all sirtuin genes (SIRT1-7)

Step 1: Search for genes
        ```python
        gene_ids = []
        for i in range(1, 8):
            handle = Entrez.esearch(
                db="gene",
                term=f"SIRT{i}[Gene] AND human[Organism]"
            )
            result = Entrez.read(handle)
            gene_ids.extend(result["IdList"])
        ```

Step 2: Fetch sequences
        ```python
        sequences = {}
        for gene_id in gene_ids:
            # Get linked mRNA
            handle = Entrez.elink(
                dbfrom="gene", db="nuccore", id=gene_id
            )
            links = Entrez.read(handle)
            
            if links[0]["LinkSetDb"]:
                mrna_id = links[0]["LinkSetDb"][0]["Link"][0]["Id"]
                # Fetch sequence
                seq_handle = Entrez.efetch(
                    db="nuccore", id=mrna_id,
                    rettype="fasta", retmode="text"
                )
                record = SeqIO.read(seq_handle, "fasta")
                sequences[record.id] = record
        ```

Step 3: Analyze
        ```python
        for name, record in sequences.items():
            gc = GC(record.seq)
            length = len(record.seq)
            print(f"{name}: {length} bp, {gc:.1f}% GC")
        ```

REAL APPLICATIONS:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
â€¢ Comparative analysis across gene families
â€¢ Finding conserved motifs
â€¢ Identifying regulatory elements
â€¢ Preparing input for phylogenetic analysis
```

#### C.1.2 Cross-Database Integration
```
LINKING MULTIPLE DATABASES:
â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

SCENARIO: Complete gene analysis
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

Start: Gene name "TERT"

Step 1: Get Gene ID from NCBI Gene
        â†’ Gene ID: 7015

Step 2: Get RefSeq mRNA from Gene
        â†’ NM_198253.3

Step 3: Get RefSeq Protein
        â†’ NP_937983.2

Step 4: Get UniProt ID
        â†’ O14746

Step 5: Get AlphaFold structure
        â†’ AF-O14746-F1

Step 6: Get PubMed articles
        â†’ 5000+ papers

Step 7: Get expression data from GTEx
        â†’ Low in most tissues, high in stem cells

PYTHON IMPLEMENTATION:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
def complete_gene_analysis(gene_name):
    """Get all info about a gene."""
    
    # 1. NCBI Gene
    handle = Entrez.esearch(db="gene", term=f"{gene_name}[Gene] AND human[Organism]")
    gene_id = Entrez.read(handle)["IdList"][0]
    
    # 2. Get linked databases
    links = Entrez.elink(dbfrom="gene", id=gene_id, cmd="acheck")
    linked_dbs = Entrez.read(links)
    
    # 3. Fetch protein
    protein_link = Entrez.elink(dbfrom="gene", db="protein", id=gene_id)
    protein_ids = Entrez.read(protein_link)
    
    # 4. Get PubMed links
    pubmed_link = Entrez.elink(dbfrom="gene", db="pubmed", id=gene_id)
    
    return {
        "gene_id": gene_id,
        "proteins": protein_ids,
        "literature": pubmed_link
    }
```

### C.2 USES IN GENETIC ENGINEERING

#### C.2.1 CRISPR Target Design
```
DESIGNING CRISPR EXPERIMENTS:
â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

WORKFLOW:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

1ï¸âƒ£ FETCH TARGET GENE SEQUENCE
   ```python
   # Get TERT gene sequence
   handle = Entrez.efetch(
       db="nuccore",
       id="NG_009265.1",  # TERT genomic sequence
       rettype="fasta"
   )
   gene_record = SeqIO.read(handle, "fasta")
   gene_seq = str(gene_record.seq)
   ```

2ï¸âƒ£ FIND PAM SITES (NGG for SpCas9)
   ```python
   import re
   
   pam_sites = []
   for match in re.finditer(r'.{20}[ATGC]GG', gene_seq):
       guide = match.group()[:-3]  # 20bp before PAM
       position = match.start()
       pam_sites.append((position, guide))
   
   print(f"Found {len(pam_sites)} potential gRNA sites")
   ```

3ï¸âƒ£ CHECK OFF-TARGETS (BLAST)
   ```python
   from Bio.Blast import NCBIWWW
   
   def check_off_targets(guide_sequence):
       result = NCBIWWW.qblast(
           "blastn", "nt", guide_sequence,
           entrez_query="homo sapiens[organism]",
           word_size=7
       )
       # Parse and count significant hits...
   ```

4ï¸âƒ£ SCORE AND RANK GUIDES
   Based on:
   â”œâ”€â”€ Off-target count (fewer = better)
   â”œâ”€â”€ GC content (40-60% ideal)
   â”œâ”€â”€ No poly-T (termination signal)
   â””â”€â”€ Position in gene (exon hits preferred)
```

#### C.2.2 Construct Design
```
DESIGNING EXPRESSION CONSTRUCTS:
â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

SCENARIO: Create TERT expression vector
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

1ï¸âƒ£ FETCH CODING SEQUENCE
   ```python
   # Get TERT CDS
   handle = Entrez.efetch(
       db="nuccore",
       id="NM_198253",
       rettype="gb",
       retmode="text"
   )
   record = SeqIO.read(handle, "genbank")
   
   # Extract CDS feature
   for feature in record.features:
       if feature.type == "CDS":
           cds_seq = feature.extract(record.seq)
           break
   ```

2ï¸âƒ£ OPTIMIZE CODONS (for expression host)
   ```python
   from Bio.SeqUtils.CodonUsage import CodonAdaptationIndex
   
   # Check codon usage
   cai = CodonAdaptationIndex()
   # Compare to E. coli codon table...
   ```

3ï¸âƒ£ ADD TAGS AND ELEMENTS
   ```python
   # Design construct
   construct = (
       "ATGCAT"  # Kozak sequence
       + str(cds_seq)  # Your gene
       + "GGAGGAGGAGGA"  # Flexible linker
       + "ATGGTGAGC..."  # GFP for visualization
   )
   ```

4ï¸âƒ£ CHECK FOR PROBLEMS
   â”œâ”€â”€ Restriction sites that conflict with cloning
   â”œâ”€â”€ Secondary structure in mRNA
   â”œâ”€â”€ Rare codons
   â””â”€â”€ Cryptic splice sites
```

### C.3 USES IN IMMORTALITY RESEARCH

#### C.3.1 Building Aging Gene Databases
```
CREATING YOUR OWN AGING DATABASE:
â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

GOAL: Compile all known aging genes with sequences
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

Step 1: DOWNLOAD GENAGE GENES
        ```python
        import pandas as pd
        
        # GenAge provides downloadable CSV
        genage = pd.read_csv("human_genes.csv")
        print(f"Found {len(genage)} aging genes")
        ```

Step 2: FETCH SEQUENCES FROM NCBI
        ```python
        gene_sequences = {}
        
        for idx, row in genage.iterrows():
            gene_name = row['symbol']
            
            # Search for gene
            handle = Entrez.esearch(
                db="gene",
                term=f"{gene_name}[Gene] AND human[Organism]"
            )
            result = Entrez.read(handle)
            
            if result["IdList"]:
                gene_id = result["IdList"][0]
                
                # Get mRNA sequence
                link_handle = Entrez.elink(
                    dbfrom="gene",
                    db="nuccore",
                    id=gene_id,
                    linkname="gene_nuccore_refseqrna"
                )
                # ... fetch and store
            
            time.sleep(0.34)  # Rate limit
        ```

Step 3: ANALYZE PATTERNS
        ```python
        # What do aging genes have in common?
        for name, seq in gene_sequences.items():
            gc = GC(seq)
            length = len(seq)
            # Look for conserved motifs...
        ```

Step 4: CROSS-REFERENCE WITH VARIANTS
        Link to ClinVar, gnomAD for population data
        Identify variants associated with longevity
```

#### C.3.2 Comparative Longevity Analysis
```
COMPARING LONGEVITY GENES ACROSS SPECIES:
â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

GOAL: Find what makes long-lived species different
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

SPECIES OF INTEREST:
â”œâ”€â”€ Bowhead whale (200+ years)
â”œâ”€â”€ Naked mole rat (30+ years, cancer resistant)
â”œâ”€â”€ Greenland shark (400+ years)
â”œâ”€â”€ Human (80-120 years)
â”œâ”€â”€ Mouse (3 years, reference)

WORKFLOW:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

1ï¸âƒ£ FETCH ORTHOLOGOUS GENES
   ```python
   longevity_genes = ["TERT", "SIRT1", "TP53", "FOXO3"]
   
   species = {
       "human": "9606",       # NCBI taxonomy ID
       "mouse": "10090",
       "naked_mole_rat": "10181",
       "bowhead_whale": "9773"
   }
   
   sequences = {}
   for gene in longevity_genes:
       for species_name, tax_id in species.items():
           handle = Entrez.esearch(
               db="gene",
               term=f"{gene}[Gene] AND txid{tax_id}[Organism]"
           )
           # Fetch sequences...
   ```

2ï¸âƒ£ ALIGN AND COMPARE
   ```python
   from Bio.Align import PairwiseAligner
   
   aligner = PairwiseAligner()
   
   # Compare human SIRT1 to bowhead SIRT1
   alignment = aligner.align(human_sirt1, whale_sirt1)
   
   # Identify unique differences in long-lived species
   ```

3ï¸âƒ£ IDENTIFY PATTERNS
   Questions to answer:
   â”œâ”€â”€ Do long-lived species have longer TERT?
   â”œâ”€â”€ Are there unique domains in long-lived species?
   â”œâ”€â”€ What's different about their p53?
   â””â”€â”€ Conservation of epigenetic regulators?

IMMORTALITY INSIGHTS:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
This approach has revealed:
â”œâ”€â”€ Naked mole rat has unique INK4 gene arrangement
â”œâ”€â”€ Bowhead whale has enhanced DNA repair genes
â”œâ”€â”€ Long-lived species often have more p53 copies
â””â”€â”€ Telomerase is regulated differently
```

## ğŸ”· MODULE 5: GENOMICS & VARIANTS (Month 5)

### 5.1 VARIANT TYPES
```
5.1.1 Single Nucleotide Variants
â”œâ”€â”€ SNP (polymorphism, >1% population)
â”œâ”€â”€ SNV (any single change)
â””â”€â”€ Synonymous vs Non-synonymous

5.1.2 Insertions/Deletions (Indels)
â”œâ”€â”€ Small (1-50 bp)
â”œâ”€â”€ Frameshift if not multiple of 3
â””â”€â”€ In-frame insertions/deletions

5.1.3 Structural Variants
â”œâ”€â”€ CNV (copy number variation)
â”œâ”€â”€ Inversions
â”œâ”€â”€ Translocations
â””â”€â”€ Large deletions/insertions
```

### 5.2 VARIANT EFFECT PREDICTION
```
5.2.1 Impact Categories
â”œâ”€â”€ HIGH (loss of function)
â”œâ”€â”€ MODERATE (missense)
â”œâ”€â”€ LOW (synonymous)
â””â”€â”€ MODIFIER (non-coding)

5.2.2 Prediction Tools
â”œâ”€â”€ SIFT (sequence-based)
â”œâ”€â”€ PolyPhen-2 (structure-based)
â”œâ”€â”€ CADD (combined score)
â””â”€â”€ ğŸ¯ AlphaGenome (AI-based)

5.2.3 âš ï¸ IMMORTALITY: Predict aging variant effects
```

### 5.3 VCF FORMAT
```
5.3.1 VCF Structure
â”œâ”€â”€ Header lines (##)
â”œâ”€â”€ Column headers
â”œâ”€â”€ CHROM, POS, REF, ALT
â””â”€â”€ QUAL, FILTER, INFO

5.3.2 VCF Processing
â”œâ”€â”€ bcftools
â”œâ”€â”€ vcftools
â”œâ”€â”€ PyVCF
â””â”€â”€ Filtering strategies
```

### 5.4 GWAS BASICS
```
5.4.1 Genome-Wide Association
â”œâ”€â”€ Case-control studies
â”œâ”€â”€ Millions of variants tested
â”œâ”€â”€ Statistical significance

5.4.2 GWAS Output
â”œâ”€â”€ Manhattan plots
â”œâ”€â”€ P-values
â”œâ”€â”€ Effect sizes (odds ratio)
â””â”€â”€ Lead SNPs

5.4.3 Longevity GWAS
â”œâ”€â”€ APOE (strongest signal)
â”œâ”€â”€ FOXO3
â”œâ”€â”€ TERT
â””â”€â”€ LPA
```

## ğŸ—ºï¸ PART A: ROADMAP (30%) - Learning Path & Order

### A.1 WEEK 1: Variant Fundamentals (Days 1-7)
```
ğŸ“… Day 1-2: Understanding Variants
â”œâ”€â”€ Morning (2 hours)
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Learn: What is a genetic variant?
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Any difference from reference genome
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Not all variants are mutations
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Most are harmless (polymorphisms)
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Some cause disease or traits
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Understand: Reference genome
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ GRCh38 (hg38) - current human reference
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ GRCh37 (hg19) - still used in some studies
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Reference is NOT "normal" - just a standard
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Coordinates depend on reference version
â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€ Afternoon (2 hours)
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Study: SNPs vs SNVs
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ SNP = Single Nucleotide Polymorphism
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Found in >1% of population
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ SNV = Single Nucleotide Variant
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Any single base change
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Example: rs1234567 (dbSNP ID)
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Practice: Look up SNPs in dbSNP
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/snp/
â”‚
â””â”€â”€ Evening (1 hour)
    â”œâ”€â”€ Explore: APOE variants and Alzheimer's
    â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ rs429358, rs7412
    â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ E2/E3/E4 alleles
    â”‚   â””â”€â”€ E4 = increased risk
    â””â”€â”€ Note: Same variant, different effects

ğŸ“… Day 3-4: Types of Variants
â”œâ”€â”€ Morning (2 hours)
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Study: Variant classification by size
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ SNV: Single base change
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Indel: 1-50bp insertion/deletion
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Structural: >50bp changes
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Copy Number: Gains/losses of segments
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Examples of each type
â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€ Afternoon (2 hours)
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Study: Variant classification by effect
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ SYNONYMOUS (silent)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Same amino acid (codon wobble)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ MISSENSE (non-synonymous)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Different amino acid
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ NONSENSE
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Creates stop codon
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ FRAMESHIFT
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Indel not divisible by 3
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ SPLICE SITE
â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Affects exon/intron boundaries
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Practice: Predict effect of variants
â”‚
â””â”€â”€ Evening (1 hour)
    â”œâ”€â”€ Review: Variant nomenclature
    â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ c.123A>G (coding DNA)
    â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ p.Val123Ile (protein)
    â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ chr1:12345:A:G (genomic)
    â””â”€â”€ Practice reading variant descriptions

ğŸ“… Day 5-6: Variant Databases
â”œâ”€â”€ Morning (2 hours)
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Explore: dbSNP
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ All known SNPs/indels
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ rs numbers as identifiers
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Allele frequencies by population
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Explore: ClinVar
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Clinical significance
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Pathogenic/Likely pathogenic
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ VUS (Variant of Uncertain Significance)
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Benign/Likely benign
â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€ Afternoon (2 hours)
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Study: gnomAD
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Population frequencies
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 140,000+ exomes
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 76,000+ genomes
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Constraint metrics (pLI, LOEUF)
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Practice: Look up aging-related variants
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Search TERT, FOXO3, APOE variants
â”‚
â””â”€â”€ Evening (1 hour)
    â”œâ”€â”€ Learn: LongevityMap database
    â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Variants associated with longevity
    â”œâ”€â”€ Cross-reference with ClinVar
    â””â”€â”€ Start building variant list

ğŸ“… Day 7: Week 1 Integration
â”œâ”€â”€ Morning (2 hours)

â”‚

### A.2 WEEK 2: VCF Format & Processing (Days 8-14)
```
ğŸ“… Day 8-9: VCF Structure
â”œâ”€â”€ Morning (2 hours)
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Learn: VCF file structure
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Meta-information lines (##)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ ##fileformat=VCFv4.2
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ ##INFO=<...>
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ ##FORMAT=<...>
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Header line (#CHROM POS ID...)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Data lines (actual variants)
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Study: Main columns
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ CHROM: Chromosome
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ POS: Position (1-based)
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ ID: Variant ID (rs number or .)
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ REF: Reference allele
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ ALT: Alternate allele(s)
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ QUAL: Quality score
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ FILTER: Pass or filter reason
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ INFO: Annotation info
â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€ Afternoon (2 hours)
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Study: INFO field contents
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ AF: Allele frequency
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ DP: Read depth
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ AC: Allele count
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Custom annotations
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Practice: Read VCF files manually
â”‚
â””â”€â”€ Evening (1 hour)
    â”œâ”€â”€ Download sample VCF
    â”œâ”€â”€ Explore structure
    â””â”€â”€ Preview: Genotype fields

ğŸ“… Day 10-11: VCF Processing with Python
â”œâ”€â”€ Morning (2 hours)
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Install: PyVCF or cyvcf2
â”‚   â”‚   ```python
â”‚   â”‚   # Option 1: PyVCF (simpler)
â”‚   â”‚   pip install PyVCF
â”‚   â”‚   
â”‚   â”‚   # Option 2: cyvcf2 (faster)
â”‚   â”‚   pip install cyvcf2
â”‚   â”‚   ```
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Basic parsing:
â”‚       ```python
â”‚       import vcf
â”‚       
â”‚       reader = vcf.Reader(filename='variants.vcf')
â”‚       for record in reader:
â”‚           print(f"{record.CHROM}:{record.POS}")
â”‚           print(f"  REF: {record.REF}")
â”‚           print(f"  ALT: {record.ALT}")
â”‚       ```
â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€ Afternoon (2 hours)
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Study: Filtering variants
â”‚   â”‚   ```python
â”‚   â”‚   # Keep only PASS variants
â”‚   â”‚   passed = [r for r in reader if r.FILTER == [] or r.FILTER is None]
â”‚   â”‚   
â”‚   â”‚   # Keep only rare variants (AF < 1%)
â”‚   â”‚   rare = [r for r in reader if r.INFO.get('AF', [1])[0] < 0.01]
â”‚   â”‚   ```
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Practice: Write filtered VCF
â”‚
â””â”€â”€ Evening (1 hour)
    â”œâ”€â”€ Build: Variant filter script
    â”œâ”€â”€ Filter by quality, frequency
    â””â”€â”€ Export filtered variants

## ğŸ“– PART B: EXPLANATION (30%) - Deep Theory

### B.1 VARIANT BIOLOGY

#### B.1.1 How Variants Arise
```
SOURCES OF GENETIC VARIATION:
â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

1ï¸âƒ£ REPLICATION ERRORS
   â”œâ”€â”€ DNA polymerase makes mistakes
   â”œâ”€â”€ ~1 error per 10â· nucleotides
   â”œâ”€â”€ Proofreading fixes most
   â””â”€â”€ Some escape â†’ mutations

2ï¸âƒ£ SPONTANEOUS DAMAGE
   â”œâ”€â”€ Depurination (loss of A/G base)
   â”œâ”€â”€ Deamination (Câ†’U, causing Câ†’T)
   â”œâ”€â”€ Oxidative damage (8-oxoG)
   â””â”€â”€ ~10,000 lesions per cell per day!

3ï¸âƒ£ ENVIRONMENTAL DAMAGE
   â”œâ”€â”€ UV radiation (pyrimidine dimers)
   â”œâ”€â”€ Ionizing radiation (strand breaks)
   â”œâ”€â”€ Chemical mutagens
   â””â”€â”€ Reactive oxygen species

4ï¸âƒ£ RECOMBINATION
   â”œâ”€â”€ Meiotic crossing-over
   â”œâ”€â”€ Creates new allele combinations
   â””â”€â”€ Source of indels and CNVs

NEW MUTATIONS PER GENERATION:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Each person has ~60-80 NEW mutations
â”œâ”€â”€ Most are neutral
â”œâ”€â”€ ~1-2 might be functional
â”œâ”€â”€ Very few are disease-causing
â””â”€â”€ Accumulate over generations!

âš ï¸ IMMORTALITY CONNECTION:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Aging involves SOMATIC mutation accumulation:
â”œâ”€â”€ Cancer driver mutations
â”œâ”€â”€ Clonal hematopoiesis (CHIP)
â”œâ”€â”€ Telomere-related variants
â””â”€â”€ DNA repair gene variants
```

#### B.1.2 Variant Effects on Proteins
```
HOW VARIANTS AFFECT PROTEIN FUNCTION:
â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

SYNONYMOUS (SILENT):
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
DNA:    GCT â†’ GCC (both code for Alanine)
Protein: Ala â†’ Ala (no change)

BUT! Not always truly silent:
â”œâ”€â”€ Can affect mRNA stability
â”œâ”€â”€ Can affect codon usage (translation speed)
â”œâ”€â”€ Can create/destroy splice sites
â””â”€â”€ Can affect mRNA folding

MISSENSE (AMINO ACID CHANGE):
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
DNA:    GCT â†’ GAT
Protein: Ala â†’ Asp (Alanine â†’ Aspartic acid)

Effect depends on:
â”œâ”€â”€ Location in protein
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Active site = usually damaging
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Surface = often tolerated
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Core = depends on size change
â”œâ”€â”€ Property change
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Same properties = conservative
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Different properties = non-conservative
â””â”€â”€ Conservation
    â””â”€â”€ Conserved positions = important

NONSENSE (STOP CODON):
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
DNA:    TGG â†’ TGA (Trp â†’ STOP)
Protein: Truncated!

Effects:
â”œâ”€â”€ Nonsense-mediated decay (NMD)
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ mRNA destroyed if stop > 50bp before last exon
â”œâ”€â”€ If escapes NMD:
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Truncated protein (usually non-functional)
â””â”€â”€ Early stops = complete loss of function

FRAMESHIFT:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
DNA:    ATG GAT CGT... â†’ ATG _AT CGT... (1 bp deletion)
        Met Asp Arg     Met Ile Leu...

Reading frame shifted:
â”œâ”€â”€ All downstream amino acids wrong
â”œâ”€â”€ Usually hits premature stop
â””â”€â”€ Complete loss of function

VISUAL EXAMPLE:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Normal:  THE CAT SAT OUT
1 del:   THE _AT SAT OUT â†’ THE ATS ATO UT (nonsense)
```

### B.2 VCF FORMAT DEEP DIVE

#### B.2.1 Complete VCF Structure
```
VCF FILE ANATOMY:
â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

##fileformat=VCFv4.2                    â† Version
##contig=<ID=chr1,length=248956422>     â† Chromosome info
##INFO=<ID=AF,Number=A,Type=Float,...>  â† INFO field definitions
##FORMAT=<ID=GT,Number=1,Type=String,..>â† Genotype format
#CHROM  POS     ID      REF ALT  QUAL FILTER INFO        FORMAT  SAMPLE1
chr1    12345   rs123   A   G    30   PASS   AF=0.15     GT:DP   0/1:25

COLUMN BREAKDOWN:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

CHROM: Chromosome name
       chr1, chr2, ..., chrX, chrY, chrM

POS:   Position (1-based, leftmost)
       12345 means the 12345th nucleotide

ID:    Variant identifier
       rs123456 (dbSNP) or . (novel)

REF:   Reference allele
       What the reference genome has
       Must match reference at this position!

ALT:   Alternate allele(s)
       G (single)
       G,T (multiple alts possible)

QUAL:  Phred-scaled quality
       30 = 99.9% confident
       50 = 99.999% confident

FILTER: Filter status
        PASS = passed all filters
        LowQual = reason for filtering

INFO:  Semicolon-separated annotations
       AF=0.15;DP=100;AC=2

GENOTYPE FIELDS:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
FORMAT: Describes genotype columns
        GT:DP:GQ = Genotype:Depth:Quality

SAMPLE: Actual genotypes
        0/0 = Homozygous reference
        0/1 = Heterozygous
        1/1 = Homozygous alternate
        1/2 = Heterozygous for two alts
        
        Example: 0/1:25:30
        Genotype: Heterozygous
        Depth: 25 reads
        Quality: 30
```

### B.3 GWAS STATISTICS

#### B.3.1 Understanding GWAS Output
```
GWAS STATISTICAL CONCEPTS:
â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

ODDS RATIO (OR):
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Measures association strength

OR = 1.0  â†’ No association
OR > 1.0  â†’ Increases risk
OR < 1.0  â†’ Decreases risk (protective)

Example: APOE E4 and Alzheimer's
OR = 3.5 â†’ E4 carriers have 3.5x higher odds

For longevity variants:
FOXO3 rs2802292 G allele:
OR = 0.7 for mortality â†’ Protective!

P-VALUE & SIGNIFICANCE:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Problem: Testing millions of variants
         If p < 0.05, expect 50,000 false positives!

Solution: Multiple testing correction
          Genome-wide significance: p < 5Ã—10â»â¸
          
Why 5Ã—10â»â¸?
â”œâ”€â”€ ~1 million independent tests
â”œâ”€â”€ Bonferroni: 0.05 / 1,000,000 = 5Ã—10â»â¸
â””â”€â”€ Conservative but standard

MANHATTAN PLOT:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Visual representation of GWAS results

Y-axis: -log10(p-value)
        Higher = more significant
        Red line at 7.3 (p = 5Ã—10â»â¸)

X-axis: Chromosomal position
        Alternating colors per chromosome

Peaks = significant associations
        "Manhattan skyline" appearance

EXAMPLE READING:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Peak at chr19 position 45,411,941
â”œâ”€â”€ -log10(p) = 50 â†’ p = 10â»âµâ° (very significant!)
â”œâ”€â”€ Contains APOE gene
â”œâ”€â”€ SNP rs429358
â”œâ”€â”€ OR = 3.5 for Alzheimer's
â””â”€â”€ Most replicated GWAS finding
```
