---

## ğŸ—ºï¸ PART A: ROADMAP (30%) - Learning Path & Order

### A.1 WEEK 1: Telomere Biology Fundamentals (Days 1-7)
```
ğŸ“… Day 1-2: Telomere Structure
â”œâ”€â”€ Morning (2 hours)
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Learn: What are telomeres?
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Protective caps on chromosome ends
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ TTAGGG repeat sequence (humans)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Length: ~10-15 kb at birth
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Shorten with each cell division
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ "Molecular clock" of aging
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Study: Telomere architecture
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Double-stranded repeats
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ 3' G-rich overhang (150-200nt)
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ T-loop: folds back, hides end
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ D-loop: strand invasion structure
â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€ Afternoon (2 hours)
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Learn: Shelterin complex
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ TRF1: Binds ds TTAGGG, negative regulator
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ TRF2: Protects ends, prevents fusion
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ POT1: Binds ss overhang
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ TIN2: Bridges TRF1-TRF2-TPP1
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ TPP1: Recruits telomerase
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ RAP1: TRF2 interactor
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Understand: Why shelterin matters
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Protects from DNA damage response
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Without it: Chromosome fusions!
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Dysregulation â†’ Cancer or senescence
â”‚
â””â”€â”€ Evening (1 hour)
    â”œâ”€â”€ Visualize T-loop/D-loop structure
    â”œâ”€â”€ Research shelterin mutations in disease
    â””â”€â”€ Preview: End replication problem

ğŸ“… Day 3-4: End Replication Problem
â”œâ”€â”€ Morning (2 hours)
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Learn: The problem
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ DNA polymerase needs RNA primer
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Primer removed at 5' end
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Gap cannot be filled
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Result: ~50-200bp lost per division
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Understand: Hayflick limit
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ ~50-70 divisions maximum
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Then: Critically short telomeres
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Trigger: p53/p21 â†’ Senescence
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ This IS cellular aging!
â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€ Afternoon (2 hours)
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Learn: Telomerase solution
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ TERT: Catalytic subunit (reverse transcriptase)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ TERC: RNA template component
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Extends 3' overhang
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Normal polymerase fills complement
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Net result: Telomere maintenance
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Note: Expression pattern
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ High in: Stem cells, germ cells
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Low in: Most somatic cells
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Reactivated in: Cancer (90%)
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ âš ï¸ IMMORTALITY KEY: Reactivate safely!
â”‚
â””â”€â”€ Evening (1 hour)
    â”œâ”€â”€ Draw end replication diagram
    â”œâ”€â”€ Research telomerase structure
    â””â”€â”€ Preview: Measurement methods

ğŸ“… Day 5-6: Telomere Measurement
â”œâ”€â”€ Morning (2 hours)
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Learn: TRF (Terminal Restriction Fragment)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Gold standard (Southern blot)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Digest DNA, probe telomeres
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Get length distribution
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Labor-intensive, needs lots of DNA
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Learn: qPCR method
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ T/S ratio (Telomere/Single copy gene)
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Relative measurement
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Fast, high-throughput
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Most common in research
â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€ Afternoon (2 hours)
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Practice: Analyze telomere data
â”‚   â”‚   ```python
â”‚   â”‚   import numpy as np
â”‚   â”‚   
â”‚   â”‚   def calculate_ts_ratio(telomere_ct, scg_ct, ref_tel, ref_scg):
â”‚   â”‚       \"\"\"Calculate Telomere/Single-copy gene ratio.\"\"\"
â”‚   â”‚       delta_tel = ref_tel - telomere_ct
â”‚   â”‚       delta_scg = ref_scg - scg_ct
â”‚   â”‚       delta_delta = delta_tel - delta_scg
â”‚   â”‚       ts_ratio = 2 ** delta_delta
â”‚   â”‚       return ts_ratio
â”‚   â”‚   
â”‚   â”‚   def estimate_telomere_length(ts_ratio, calibration=None):
â”‚   â”‚       \"\"\"Convert T/S to approximate length in kb.\"\"\"
â”‚   â”‚       if calibration:
â”‚   â”‚           return calibration(ts_ratio)
â”‚   â”‚       # Rough estimate: T/S ~1.0 â‰ˆ 6-7kb
â”‚   â”‚       return ts_ratio * 6.5
â”‚   â”‚   ```
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Learn: Other methods
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Flow-FISH: Single cell resolution
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ STELA: Individual chromosome telomeres
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Nanopore: Direct sequencing
â”‚
â””â”€â”€ Evening (1 hour)
    â”œâ”€â”€ Compare method advantages
    â”œâ”€â”€ Practice data interpretation
    â””â”€â”€ Preview: Telomere extension

â”‚   â”‚   ```python
â”‚   â”‚   class TelomereTherapyMonitor:
â”‚   â”‚       def __init__(self, patient_id):
â”‚   â”‚           self.patient_id = patient_id
â”‚   â”‚           self.measurements = []
â”‚   â”‚       
â”‚   â”‚       def add_measurement(self, date, ts_ratio, method='qPCR'):
â”‚   â”‚           self.measurements.append({
â”‚   â”‚               'date': date,
â”‚   â”‚               'ts_ratio': ts_ratio,
â”‚   â”‚               'length_kb': ts_ratio * 6.5,
â”‚   â”‚               'method': method
â”‚   â”‚           })
â”‚   â”‚       
â”‚   â”‚       def check_safety(self):
â”‚   â”‚           if not self.measurements:
â”‚   â”‚               return {'status': 'No data'}
â”‚   â”‚           
â”‚   â”‚           current = self.measurements[-1]['length_kb']
â”‚   â”‚           
â”‚   â”‚           if current > 15:
â”‚   â”‚               return {'status': 'WARNING - Too long!',
â”‚   â”‚                       'action': 'Consider stopping therapy'}
â”‚   â”‚           elif current < 5:
â”‚   â”‚               return {'status': 'CRITICAL - Too short',
â”‚   â”‚                       'action': 'Increase therapy'}
â”‚   â”‚           else:
â”‚   â”‚               return {'status': 'Normal',
â”‚   â”‚                       'action': 'Continue monitoring'}
â”‚   â”‚   ```
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Study: Current clinical landscape
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Libella Gene Therapeutics
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Telocyte (TAT2)

## ğŸ“– PART B: EXPLANATION (30%) - Deep Theory

### B.1 TELOMERE BIOLOGY

#### B.1.1 Molecular Structure
```
TELOMERE ARCHITECTURE:
â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

SEQUENCE:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
5'...â”€â”€â”€[TTAGGG]nâ”€â”€â”€â†’ 3' overhang
        â†‘

                    T-Loop

#### B.1.2 Telomerase Mechanism
```
TELOMERASE ACTION:
â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

COMPONENTS:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
TERT: Telomerase Reverse Transcriptase
      â”œâ”€â”€ Catalytic core (RT domain)
      â”œâ”€â”€ RNA binding domain
      â””â”€â”€ Adds nucleotides using TERC template

TERC: Telomerase RNA Component
      â”œâ”€â”€ 451 nucleotides (human)
      â”œâ”€â”€ Contains template: 3'-CAAUCCCAAUC-5'
      â””â”€â”€ Scaffold for TERT

MECHANISM:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Step 1: Recognition
        TERT + TERC complex binds 3' overhang
        â”‚
        â–¼
Step 2: Hybridization
        Template pairs with telomere end
        ...TTAGGG-3'
           â”‚â”‚â”‚â”‚â”‚
        5'-AAUCCC-3' (template)
        â”‚
        â–¼
Step 3: Extension
        TERT adds nucleotides: G-G-T-T-A-G
        â”‚
        â–¼
Step 4: Translocation
        Move template for next round
        â”‚
        â–¼
Step 5: Repeat
        Add more TTAGGG repeats
        â”‚
        â–¼
Step 6: C-strand synthesis
        Normal DNA polymerase fills gap
```

## ğŸ”¬ PART C: USES & APPLICATIONS (30%)

### C.1 TELOMERE LENGTH ANALYSIS PIPELINE
```python
import pandas as pd
import numpy as np
from scipy import stats

class TelomereLengthAnalyzer:
    \"\"\"Complete telomere analysis pipeline.\"\"\"
    
    def __init__(self):
        self.reference_data = self.load_reference()
    
    def load_reference(self):
        \"\"\"Age-matched reference telomere lengths.\"\"\"
        return {
            'age_ranges': [(0, 20), (20, 40), (40, 60), (60, 80), (80, 100)],
            'mean_kb': [10.5, 8.0, 6.5, 5.0, 4.0],
            'std_kb': [1.5, 1.2, 1.0, 0.8, 0.7]
        }
    
    def calculate_biological_age(self, telomere_kb, chronological_age):
        \"\"\"Estimate biological age from telomere length.\"\"\"
        # Simple linear model (in reality, more complex)
        # Assumes 50bp loss per year
        birth_telomere = 11.0  # kb
        loss_rate = 0.05  # kb per year
        
        bio_age = (birth_telomere - telomere_kb) / loss_rate
        age_acceleration = bio_age - chronological_age
        
        return {
            'biological_age': bio_age,
            'chronological_age': chronological_age,
            'age_acceleration': age_acceleration,
            'status': 'Accelerated' if age_acceleration > 5 else 
                     'Decelerated' if age_acceleration < -5 else 'Normal'
        }
    
    def assess_intervention_need(self, telomere_kb, age):
        \"\"\"Determine if telomere intervention recommended.\"\"\"
        age_expected = 10.5 - (age * 0.05)  # Expected for age
        percentile = self.calculate_percentile(telomere_kb, age)
        
        if percentile < 10:
            return {
                'recommendation': 'URGENT - Consider intervention',
                'options': ['TERT gene therapy', 'TA-65 supplementation',
                           'Lifestyle optimization'],
                'risk_level': 'HIGH'
            }
        elif percentile < 25:
            return {
                'recommendation': 'Monitor closely',
                'options': ['Lifestyle changes', 'Quarterly monitoring'],
                'risk_level': 'MODERATE'
            }
        else:
            return {
                'recommendation': 'Continue normal monitoring',
                'options': ['Annual checkup'],
                'risk_level': 'LOW'
            }

# Usage for immortality planning
analyzer = TelomereLengthAnalyzer()
my_result = analyzer.calculate_biological_age(telomere_kb=6.0, chronological_age=16)
intervention = analyzer.assess_intervention_need(6.0, 16)
```

### D.1 KEY PAPERS
```
ESSENTIAL READING:
â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

1ï¸âƒ£ Blasco AAV-TERT (2012)
   "Telomerase gene therapy in adult mice"
   EMBO Mol Med 4:691-704
   â˜…â˜…â˜…â˜…â˜… Landmark study

2ï¸âƒ£ Horvath Telomere-Epigenetic (2018)
   "Telomere length and epigenetic age"
   Nature Genetics
   â˜…â˜…â˜…â˜…â˜† Integration

### A.1 WEEK 1: Epigenetic Fundamentals (Days 1-7)
```
ğŸ“… Day 1-2: DNA Methylation
â”œâ”€â”€ Morning (2 hours)
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Learn: What is DNA methylation?
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Addition of CH3 to cytosine
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Primarily at CpG dinucleotides
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 5-methylcytosine (5mC)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Generally silences gene expression
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ âš ï¸ CHANGES WITH AGE!
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Study: CpG islands
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Regions enriched in CpGs
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Often at promoters
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Usually unmethylated when gene active
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Methylated = Gene silenced
â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€ Afternoon (2 hours)
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Learn: Methylation machinery
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ DNMTs (DNA methyltransferases)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ DNMT1: Maintenance (copies during replication)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ DNMT3A/B: De novo (establishes new)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ DNMT3L: Cofactor
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ TETs (demethylation)
â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ TET1/2/3: 5mC â†’ 5hmC â†’ ...â†’ C
â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Active demethylation pathway
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Understand: Aging changes
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Global hypomethylation
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Local hypermethylation
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Pattern becomes "noisy"
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ This is epigenetic drift!
â”‚
â””â”€â”€ Evening (1 hour)
    â”œâ”€â”€ Research methylation patterns
    â”œâ”€â”€ Connect to gene expression
    â””â”€â”€ Preview: Histone modifications

ğŸ“… Day 3-4: Histone Modifications
â”œâ”€â”€ Morning (2 hours)
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Learn: Histone basics
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ DNA wraps around histones
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Nucleosome: 147bp + histone octamer
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ H2A, H2B, H3, H4 (core histones)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ H1: Linker histone
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ N-terminal tails stick out
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Study: Modification types
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Acetylation (Ac): Opens chromatin
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Methylation (Me): Complex effects
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Phosphorylation (P): Signaling
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Ubiquitination (Ub): Degradation signals
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Many more...
â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€ Afternoon (2 hours)
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Learn: Histone code
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ H3K4me3: Active promoters
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ H3K27ac: Active enhancers
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ H3K9me3: Heterochromatin (silent)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ H3K27me3: Polycomb repression
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Combinations matter!
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Understand: Writers, erasers, readers
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Writers: Add marks (HATs, HMTs)
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Erasers: Remove marks (HDACs, KDMs)
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Readers: Interpret marks
â”‚
â””â”€â”€ Evening (1 hour)
    â”œâ”€â”€ Visualize chromatin states
    â”œâ”€â”€ Connect to aging
    â””â”€â”€ Preview: Epigenetic clocks

ğŸ“… Day 5-6: Epigenetic Clocks
â”œâ”€â”€ Morning (2 hours)
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Learn: What are epigenetic clocks?
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Methylation patterns predict age
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ More accurate than telomeres!
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Trained on thousands of samples
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Multiple clock types exist
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ âš ï¸ BIOLOGICAL AGE GOLD STANDARD!
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Study: Major clocks
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Horvath (2013): 353 CpGs, multi-tissue
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Hannum (2013): 71 CpGs, blood
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ GrimAge (2019): Mortality predictor
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ PhenoAge: Health span focus
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ DunedinPACE: Rate of aging
â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€ Afternoon (2 hours)
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Practice: Implement epigenetic clock
â”‚   â”‚   ```python
â”‚   â”‚   import numpy as np
â”‚   â”‚   
â”‚   â”‚   class HorvathClock:
â”‚   â”‚       def __init__(self):
â”‚   â”‚           # Simplified - real clock has 353 CpGs
â”‚   â”‚           self.cpg_sites = ['cg00000292', 'cg00002426', ...]
â”‚   â”‚           self.coefficients = [...]  # From Horvath paper
â”‚   â”‚           self.intercept = 0.0
â”‚   â”‚       
â”‚   â”‚       def predict_age(self, methylation_beta):
â”‚   â”‚           \"\"\"Predict DNAm age from beta values.\"\"\"
â”‚   â”‚           # Beta values: 0-1 (proportion methylated)
â”‚   â”‚           linear_pred = self.intercept
â”‚   â”‚           for cpg, coef in zip(self.cpg_sites, self.coefficients):
â”‚   â”‚               if cpg in methylation_beta:
â”‚   â”‚                   linear_pred += coef * methylation_beta[cpg]
â”‚   â”‚           
â”‚   â”‚           # Transform (anti-trafo)
â”‚   â”‚           if linear_pred < 0:
â”‚   â”‚               age = (1 + adult_offset) * np.exp(linear_pred) - 1
â”‚   â”‚           else:
â”‚   â”‚               age = (1 + adult_offset) * linear_pred + adult_offset
â”‚   â”‚           
â”‚   â”‚           return age
â”‚   â”‚       
â”‚   â”‚       def calculate_age_acceleration(self, dnam_age, chron_age):
â”‚   â”‚           return dnam_age - chron_age
â”‚   â”‚   ```
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Learn: Clock interpretation
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Positive acceleration = Older biologically
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Negative acceleration = Younger biologically
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ GrimAge: Best mortality predictor
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ DunedinPACE: Measures RATE of aging
â”‚
â””â”€â”€ Evening (1 hour)
    â”œâ”€â”€ Compare different clocks
    â”œâ”€â”€ Research validation studies
    â””â”€â”€ Preview: Epigenetic editing

ğŸ“… Day 10-11: Targeted Epigenetic Editing
â”œâ”€â”€ Morning (2 hours)
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Learn: dCas9 epigenetic tools
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ dCas9-DNMT3A: Add methylation
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ dCas9-TET1: Remove methylation

â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ CRISPRoff: Stable silencing

â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Find age-associated CpGs
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Young pattern: Target methylation state
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Design gRNAs
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Predict clock reversal
â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€ Afternoon (2 hours)
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Practice: Epigenetic editor design
â”‚   â”‚   ```python
â”‚   â”‚   class EpigeneticEditor:
â”‚   â”‚       \"\"\"Design dCas9-based epigenetic editors.\"\"\"
â”‚   â”‚       
â”‚   â”‚       def __init__(self, target_cpg, desired_state):
â”‚   â”‚           self.target = target_cpg
â”‚   â”‚           self.desired = desired_state
â”‚   â”‚       
â”‚   â”‚       def select_editor(self):
â”‚   â”‚           if self.desired == 'methylated':
â”‚   â”‚               return 'dCas9-DNMT3A'
â”‚   â”‚           elif self.desired == 'unmethylated':
â”‚   â”‚               return 'dCas9-TET1'
â”‚   â”‚       
â”‚   â”‚       def design_guide(self):
â”‚   â”‚           \"\"\"Design gRNA targeting CpG region.\"\"\"
â”‚   â”‚           # Get sequence around CpG
â”‚   â”‚           sequence = get_cpg_context(self.target, window=50)
â”‚   â”‚           pam_sites = find_pam_sites(sequence)
â”‚   â”‚           
â”‚   â”‚           # Select guide within ~50bp of CpG
â”‚   â”‚           guides = []
â”‚   â”‚           for pam in pam_sites:
â”‚   â”‚               distance = abs(pam - 25)  # center is CpG
â”‚   â”‚               if distance < 50:
â”‚   â”‚                   guides.append({
â”‚   â”‚                       'position': pam,
â”‚   â”‚                       'distance_to_cpg': distance,
â”‚   â”‚                       'spacer': sequence[pam-20:pam]
â”‚   â”‚                   })
â”‚   â”‚           
â”‚   â”‚           return sorted(guides, key=lambda x: x['distance_to_cpg'])
â”‚   â”‚   
â”‚   â”‚   # Design editors for aging CpGs
â”‚   â”‚   aging_cpgs = [
â”‚   â”‚       ('cg16867657', 'unmethylated'),  # Gains methylation with age
â”‚   â”‚       ('cg10501210', 'methylated'),    # Loses methylation with age
â”‚   â”‚   ]
â”‚   â”‚   
â”‚   â”‚   for cpg, state in aging_cpgs:
â”‚   â”‚       editor = EpigeneticEditor(cpg, state)
â”‚   â”‚       print(f"CpG: {cpg}")
â”‚   â”‚       print(f"Editor: {editor.select_editor()}")
â”‚   â”‚       print(f"Guides: {editor.design_guide()[:2]}")
â”‚   â”‚   ```
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Study: CRISPRoff for stable changes
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ dCas9-DNMT3A-KRAB fusion
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Heritable silencing
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ One treatment, permanent effect
â”‚
â””â”€â”€ Evening (1 hour)
    â”œâ”€â”€ Consider multi-CpG targeting
    â”œâ”€â”€ Research efficacy data
    â””â”€â”€ Preview: Integration

ğŸ“… Day 12-13: Age Reversal Integration
â”œâ”€â”€ Morning (2 hours)

â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Code: Age reversal monitor
â”‚   â”‚   ```python

â”‚   â”‚       \"\"\"Complete biological age management.\"\"\"
â”‚   â”‚       
â”‚   â”‚       def __init__(self, patient_id):
â”‚   â”‚           self.patient = patient_id
â”‚   â”‚           self.interventions = []
â”‚   â”‚           self.measurements = {
â”‚   â”‚               'epigenetic_age': [],
â”‚   â”‚               'telomere_length': [],
â”‚   â”‚               'grimace': [],
â”‚   â”‚               'dunedin_pace': []
â”‚   â”‚           }
â”‚   â”‚       
â”‚   â”‚       def baseline_assessment(self):
â”‚   â”‚           \"\"\"Initial biological age assessment.\"\"\"
â”‚   â”‚           return {
â”‚   â”‚               'horvath_age': measure_horvath(),
â”‚   â”‚               'grimace': measure_grimace(),
â”‚   â”‚               'pace': measure_dunedin_pace(),
â”‚   â”‚               'telomere_kb': measure_telomere(),
â”‚   â”‚               'chronological_age': get_age(self.patient)
â”‚   â”‚           }
â”‚   â”‚       
â”‚   â”‚       def design_intervention(self, baseline):
â”‚   â”‚           \"\"\"Design personalized intervention.\"\"\"
â”‚   â”‚           plan = []
â”‚   â”‚           
â”‚   â”‚           # Telomere intervention
â”‚   â”‚           if baseline['telomere_kb'] < 5:
â”‚   â”‚               plan.append({
â”‚   â”‚                   'type': 'Telomere extension',
â”‚   â”‚                   'method': 'AAV-TERT or CRISPRa',
â”‚   â”‚                   'priority': 'HIGH'
â”‚   â”‚               })
â”‚   â”‚           
â”‚   â”‚           # Epigenetic intervention
â”‚   â”‚           age_accel = baseline['horvath_age'] - baseline['chronological_age']
â”‚   â”‚           if age_accel > 5:
â”‚   â”‚               plan.append({
â”‚   â”‚                   'type': 'Epigenetic reset',
â”‚   â”‚                   'method': 'Partial reprogramming (OSK)',
â”‚   â”‚                   'priority': 'HIGH'
â”‚   â”‚               })
â”‚   â”‚           
â”‚   â”‚           return plan
â”‚   â”‚       
â”‚   â”‚       def track_progress(self, new_measurement):
â”‚   â”‚           \"\"\"Track biological age over time.\"\"\"
â”‚   â”‚           for key, value in new_measurement.items():
â”‚   â”‚               if key in self.measurements:
â”‚   â”‚                   self.measurements[key].append({
â”‚   â”‚                       'date': datetime.now(),
â”‚   â”‚                       'value': value
â”‚   â”‚                   })
â”‚   â”‚           
â”‚   â”‚           # Check for reversal
â”‚   â”‚           if len(self.measurements['epigenetic_age']) >= 2:
â”‚   â”‚               change = (self.measurements['epigenetic_age'][-1]['value'] -
â”‚   â”‚                        self.measurements['epigenetic_age'][-2]['value'])
â”‚   â”‚               return {
â”‚   â”‚                   'age_change': change,
â”‚   â”‚                   'direction': 'REVERSED!' if change < 0 else 'Aging'
â”‚   â”‚               }
â”‚   â”‚   ```
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Study: Current clinical trials

## ğŸ“– PART B: EXPLANATION (30%) - Deep Theory

### B.1 EPIGENETIC AGING

#### B.1.1 The Aging Methylome
```
METHYLATION CHANGES WITH AGE:
â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

GLOBAL PATTERN:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
                    Young             Old
Global methylation: â–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆ      â–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ–‘â–‘â–‘â–‘
                    (high)            (lower - hypomethylated)

Specific CpGs:      
Some gain:          â–“â–‘â–‘â–‘              â–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆ
                    (low)             (high - hypermethylated)

                    (high)            (low)

PATTERN = EPIGENETIC DRIFT

CLOCK CpGs:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Not random changes! Specific CpGs change predictably.

Horvath's 353 CpGs:
â”œâ”€â”€ Some correlate positively with age (gain methylation)
â”œâ”€â”€ Some correlate negatively (lose methylation)
â”œâ”€â”€ Combined = Accurate age prediction
â””â”€â”€ Error: ~3.6 years

GrimAge adds:
â”œâ”€â”€ Plasma protein surrogates (from methylation)
â”œâ”€â”€ Smoking pack-years
â”œâ”€â”€ Predicts TIME TO DEATH
â””â”€â”€ Most important clinical clock

### B.2 REPROGRAMMING BIOLOGY

```
PARTIAL REPROGRAMMING MECHANISM:
â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

FULL REPROGRAMMING (iPSC):
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Somatic Cell â†’ Intermediate â†’ iPSC
   â”‚                            â”‚
   â”œâ”€â”€ Adult methylome          â”œâ”€â”€ Embryonic methylome
   â”œâ”€â”€ Cell identity            â”œâ”€â”€ Pluripotent identity
   â”œâ”€â”€ Aged epigenome           â”œâ”€â”€ "Zero" epigenetic age
   â””â”€â”€ Function                 â””â”€â”€ Can become any cell

Problem: Lost identity! Not useful for rejuvenation.

PARTIAL REPROGRAMMING:
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Somatic Cell â†’ PARTIAL â†’ Rejuvenated Cell
   â”‚             treatment        â”‚
   â”œâ”€â”€ Adult methylome   â†’  â”œâ”€â”€ Younger methylome
   â”œâ”€â”€ Cell identity     â†’  â”œâ”€â”€ SAME identity kept
   â”œâ”€â”€ Aged epigenome    â†’  â”œâ”€â”€ Partially reset
   â””â”€â”€ Function          â†’  â””â”€â”€ Improved function

Key: Stop before identity loss!
Method: Cyclic, short exposure to OSKM/OSK
```

## ğŸ”¬ PART C: USES & APPLICATIONS (30%)

### C.1 COMPLETE BIOLOGICAL AGE SYSTEM
```python
class BiologicalAgeAnalyzer:
    \"\"\"Complete system for biological age assessment and reversal.\"\"\"
    
    def __init__(self):
        self.clocks = {
            'horvath': self.horvath_clock,
            'grimace': self.grimace_clock,
            'pace': self.dunedin_pace
        }
    
    def full_assessment(self, methylation_data, telomere_ts, chron_age):
        \"\"\"Complete biological age assessment.\"\"\"
        results = {
            'chronological_age': chron_age,
            'clocks': {}
        }
        
        # Calculate all clocks
        for name, clock_fn in self.clocks.items():
            clock_age = clock_fn(methylation_data)
            results['clocks'][name] = {
                'age': clock_age,
                'acceleration': clock_age - chron_age
            }
        
        # Telomere assessment
        telomere_kb = telomere_ts * 6.5
        telomere_bio_age = (11.0 - telomere_kb) / 0.05
        results['telomere'] = {
            'length_kb': telomere_kb,
            'biological_age': telomere_bio_age,
            'acceleration': telomere_bio_age - chron_age
        }
        
        # Overall assessment
        avg_accel = np.mean([c['acceleration'] 
                            for c in results['clocks'].values()])
        results['overall'] = {
            'average_acceleration': avg_accel,
            'status': self.classify_aging(avg_accel),
            'intervention_priority': 'HIGH' if avg_accel > 5 else 
                                    'MODERATE' if avg_accel > 2 else 'LOW'
        }
        
        return results
    
    def recommend_intervention(self, assessment):
        \"\"\"Generate personalized intervention recommendations.\"\"\"
        recommendations = []
        
        # Based on overall acceleration
        if assessment['overall']['intervention_priority'] == 'HIGH':
            recommendations.append({
                'intervention': 'Partial reprogramming (OSK)',
                'urgency': 'Consider clinical trial enrollment',
                'expected_effect': '5-10 year reversal possible'
            })
        
        # Telomere-specific
        if assessment['telomere']['acceleration'] > 5:
            recommendations.append({
                'intervention': 'Telomere extension',
                'options': ['AAV-TERT therapy', 'CRISPRa activation'],
                'lifestyle': ['Reduce stress', 'Exercise', 'Sleep optimization']
            })
        
        # Always include lifestyle
        recommendations.append({
            'intervention': 'Lifestyle optimization',
            'components': [
                'Caloric restriction or intermittent fasting',
                'Regular exercise (150+ min/week)',
                'Sleep 7-9 hours',
                'Stress management',
                'Consider: NAD+ precursors, metformin'
            ]
        })
        
        return recommendations

# Usage
analyzer = BiologicalAgeAnalyzer()
my_assessment = analyzer.full_assessment(
    methylation_data=my_methylation_array,
    telomere_ts=1.2,
    chron_age=16
)
intervention_plan = analyzer.recommend_intervention(my_assessment)

print("=== BIOLOGICAL AGE REPORT ===")
print(f"Chronological Age: {my_assessment['chronological_age']}")
print(f"Epigenetic Age (Horvath): {my_assessment['clocks']['horvath']['age']:.1f}")
print(f"Age Acceleration: {my_assessment['overall']['average_acceleration']:.1f} years")
print(f"Status: {my_assessment['overall']['status']}")
print(f"\\nRecommendations: {intervention_plan}")
```

ğŸ“… Day 8-9: Safety Considerations

â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Dose optimization
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Code: Safety monitoring
â”‚       ```python
â”‚       class TherapySafetyMonitor:
â”‚           def __init__(self, patient_id, therapy_type):
â”‚               self.patient = patient_id
â”‚               self.therapy = therapy_type
â”‚               self.adverse_events = []
â”‚               self.biomarkers = []
â”‚           
â”‚           def log_event(self, event_type, severity, description):
â”‚               self.adverse_events.append({
â”‚                   'date': datetime.now(),
â”‚                   'type': event_type,
â”‚                   'severity': severity,
â”‚                   'description': description
â”‚               })
â”‚               
â”‚               if severity >= 3:
â”‚                   self.trigger_alert(event_type, severity)
â”‚           
â”‚           def check_biomarkers(self, liver_enzymes, immune_markers):
â”‚               status = 'OK'
â”‚               
â”‚               if liver_enzymes['ALT'] > 3 * normal:
â”‚                   status = 'WARNING: Liver toxicity'
â”‚               
â”‚               if immune_markers['CRP'] > threshold:
â”‚                   status = 'WARNING: Inflammation'
â”‚               
â”‚               return status
â”‚       ```
â”‚
â””â”€â”€ Evening (1 hour)
    â”œâ”€â”€ Research adverse events in trials
    â”œâ”€â”€ Note regulatory requirements
    â””â”€â”€ Preview: Clinical pathway

ğŸ“… Day 10-11: Regulatory Path

â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Study: Approved gene therapies
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Luxturna (AAV-RPE65, eye)
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Zolgensma (AAV9-SMN1, SMA)
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Casgevy (CRISPR, sickle cell)
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Note: All have specific targets
â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€ Afternoon (2 hours)
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Consider: Longevity therapy path
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Challenge: "Aging" not a disease?
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Strategy: Target specific conditions

AAV (Adeno-Associated Virus):
â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

## ğŸ”¬ PART C: USES & APPLICATIONS (30%)

### C.1 COMPLETE DELIVERY DESIGN

```python
class GeneTherapyDesigner:
    """Complete gene therapy vector design pipeline."""
    
    def __init__(self, target_gene, tissue, duration):
        self.gene = target_gene
        self.tissue = tissue
        self.duration = duration  # 'permanent' or 'transient'
    
    def select_vector(self):
        """Select optimal delivery vector."""
        if self.duration == 'transient':
            return {
                'vector': 'LNP-mRNA',
                'rationale': 'Safe, repeatable, no integration',
                'suitable_for': ['OSK cycling', 'Cas9 delivery']
            }
        
        # Check gene size
        gene_size = get_gene_size(self.gene)
        
        if gene_size > 4700:
            return {
                'vector': 'Lentivirus',
                'rationale': 'Gene too large for AAV',
                'note': 'Prefer ex vivo if possible'
            }
        
        # Select AAV serotype by tissue
        serotype_map = {
            'liver': 'AAV8',
            'muscle': 'AAV1',
            'CNS': 'AAV9',
            'heart': 'AAV9',
            'eye': 'AAV2',
            'systemic': 'AAV9'
        }
        
        return {
            'vector': 'AAV',
            'serotype': serotype_map.get(self.tissue, 'AAV9'),
            'rationale': 'Optimal for in vivo, long-term expression'
        }
    
    def design_construct(self):
        """Design the genetic construct."""
        vector = self.select_vector()
        
        construct = {
            'vector': vector,
            'promoter': self.select_promoter(),
            'gene': self.gene,
            'regulatory': self.add_safety_elements(),
            'total_size': self.calculate_size()
        }
        
        return construct
    
    def add_safety_elements(self):
        """Add safety mechanisms."""
        return {
            'kill_switch': 'iCasp9 (optional)',
            'inducible': 'Tet-on system (recommended)',
            'tissue_specific': f'{self.tissue}-specific promoter',
            'monitoring': 'Include reporter (optional)'
        }

# Design TERT therapy
tert_therapy = GeneTherapyDesigner('TERT', 'systemic', 'permanent')
design = tert_therapy.design_construct()

print("TERT GENE THERAPY DESIGN")
print("=" * 50)
print(f"Vector: {design['vector']}")
print(f"Promoter: {design['promoter']}")
print(f"Safety: {design['regulatory']}")
```

### A.2 WEEK 2: AlphaGenome Integration (Days 8-14)
```
ğŸ“… Day 8-10: AI-Powered Aging Analysis

â””â”€â”€ Code: Integration pipeline
    ```python
    class ImmortalityPipeline:
        """Complete immortality research integration."""
        
        def __init__(self, genome_file=None, methylation_file=None):
            self.genome = load_vcf(genome_file) if genome_file else None
            self.methylation = load_methylation(methylation_file) if methylation_file else None
            self.interventions = []
        
        def assess_biological_age(self):
            """Complete biological age assessment."""
            results = {}
            
            if self.methylation:
                results['epigenetic_ages'] = {
                    'horvath': calculate_horvath(self.methylation),
                    'grimace': calculate_grimace(self.methylation),
                    'pace': calculate_dunedin_pace(self.methylation)
                }
            
            results['telomere_estimate'] = self.estimate_telomere_status()
            results['recommended_interventions'] = self.prioritize_interventions()
            
            return results
        
        def analyze_longevity_variants(self):
            """Check for known longevity/risk variants."""
            if not self.genome:
                return {'error': 'No genome data available'}
            
            longevity_snps = {
                'rs429358': {'gene': 'APOE', 'risk': 'E4 allele', 
                            'intervention': 'Base editing possible'},
                'rs2802292': {'gene': 'FOXO3', 'protective': 'G allele'},
                'rs2736100': {'gene': 'TERT', 'telomere_length': True}
            }
            
            results = []
            for snp, info in longevity_snps.items():
                if snp in self.genome:
                    variant = self.genome[snp]
                    results.append({
                        'snp': snp,
                        'your_genotype': variant,
                        **info,
                        'actionable': self.is_actionable(snp, variant)
                    })
            
            return results
        
        def design_intervention_panel(self):
            """Design complete intervention strategy."""
            panel = {
                'genetic': [],
                'pharmacological': [],
                'lifestyle': []
            }
            
            # Genetic interventions
            panel['genetic'] = [
                {'target': 'TERT', 'method': 'CRISPRa', 'priority': 'HIGH'},
                {'target': 'CDKN2A', 'method': 'CRISPRi', 'priority': 'MEDIUM'},
                {'target': 'OSK delivery', 'method': 'AAV/LNP', 'priority': 'RESEARCH'}
            ]
            
            # Pharmacological
            panel['pharmacological'] = [
                {'compound': 'Rapamycin', 'dose': '1-6mg/week', 'evidence': 'Strong'},
                {'compound': 'Metformin', 'dose': '500-1500mg/day', 'evidence': 'Moderate'},
                {'compound': 'NMN/NR', 'dose': '250-500mg/day', 'evidence': 'Emerging'}
            ]
            
            # Lifestyle
            panel['lifestyle'] = [
                'Time-restricted eating (16:8)',
                'Zone 2 cardio: 150+ min/week',
                'Strength training: 2-3x/week',
                'Sleep: 7-9 hours, consistent schedule',
                'Stress: Daily meditation/breathwork'
            ]
            
            return panel
        
        def generate_monitoring_schedule(self):
            """Create biomarker monitoring schedule."""
            return {
                'quarterly': [
                    'Epigenetic clock (Horvath or GrimAge)',
                    'Blood biomarkers (lipids, glucose, inflammation)'
                ],
                'annually': [
                    'Telomere length (qPCR)',
                    'Full metabolic panel',
                    'Cancer screening (age-appropriate)'
                ],
                'continuous': [
                    'HRV monitoring',
                    'Sleep tracking',
                    'Activity/exercise logging'
                ]
            }
    
    # Run the immortality pipeline
    pipeline = ImmortalityPipeline()
    
    # Get full assessment
    age_assessment = pipeline.assess_biological_age()
    variants = pipeline.analyze_longevity_variants() 
    intervention_plan = pipeline.design_intervention_panel()
    monitoring = pipeline.generate_monitoring_schedule()
    
    print("=" * 60)
    print("       PERSONAL IMMORTALITY RESEARCH PLAN")
    print("=" * 60)
    print(f"\nBiological Age Assessment: {age_assessment}")
    print(f"\nLongevity Variants: {variants}")
    print(f"\nIntervention Plan: {intervention_plan}")
    print(f"\nMonitoring Schedule: {monitoring}")
    ```

## ğŸ“‹ COMPLETE SYLLABUS SUMMARY

```

                                        (Month 1 â€¢ 1280+ Lines)
â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•
â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€ 1.1 CELL TO DNA HIERARCHY
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 1.1.1 Cell Biology Basics
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Cell = Basic unit of life (trillions in human body)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Prokaryotes vs Eukaryotes
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Prokaryote: No nucleus (bacteria)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Eukaryote: Has nucleus (humans, plants, fungi)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Cell Membrane: Phospholipid bilayer, gatekeeping
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Cytoplasm: Gel-like substance, chemical reactions
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 1.1.2 Organelles Deep Dive
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ NUCLEUS (Command Center)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Contains DNA in chromosomes
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Nuclear envelope with pores
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Nucleolus: rRNA production
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ âš ï¸ Aging: Nuclear envelope breakdown
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ MITOCHONDRIA (Powerhouse)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ ATP production via oxidative phosphorylation
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Has own DNA (mtDNA, 16.5kb)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 1000-2000 per cell
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ âš ï¸ Aging: mtDNA mutations accumulate
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ ENDOPLASMIC RETICULUM
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Rough ER: Ribosomes, protein synthesis
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Smooth ER: Lipid synthesis, detox
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ âš ï¸ Aging: ER stress increases
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ GOLGI APPARATUS
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Protein modification & packaging
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ cis (receiving) â†’ trans (shipping)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Vesicle trafficking
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ RIBOSOMES (Protein Factory)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Large + Small subunit (60S + 40S = 80S)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ A, P, E sites for tRNA
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Peptide bond formation
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Free vs ER-bound ribosomes
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ LYSOSOMES & AUTOPHAGY
â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Digestive enzymes (pH 4.5-5)
â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Autophagy: Self-eating for cleanup
â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ âš ï¸ Aging: Autophagy decline = damage accumulation
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 1.1.3 Chromosomes & Genome
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Human: 46 chromosomes (23 pairs)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 22 autosomal pairs
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ 1 sex chromosome pair (XX/XY)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Genome Size: 3.2 billion base pairs
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ ~20,000-25,000 genes (only 1.5% coding!)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Chromatin: DNA + histone proteins
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Euchromatin: Open, active
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Heterochromatin: Closed, silent
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ âš ï¸ Aging: Chromatin compaction changes
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ 1.1.4 Gene Concept
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Gene = Unit of heredity (DNA segment)
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Gene Structure:
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Promoter (control region)
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Exons (coding sequences)
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Introns (non-coding, removed)
â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ UTRs (untranslated regions)
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Alleles: Different versions of a gene
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Genotype â†’ Phenotype relationship
â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€ 1.2 DNA STRUCTURE & CHEMISTRY
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 1.2.1 Double Helix Discovery
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Watson & Crick (1953) + Franklin's X-ray
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Right-handed helix
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Major & minor grooves
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ 10.5 bp per turn, 3.4nm pitch
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 1.2.2 Nucleotide Chemistry
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Components:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Phosphate group (negative charge)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Deoxyribose sugar (5-carbon)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Nitrogenous base (A/T/G/C)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Purines (2 rings): Adenine, Guanine
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Pyrimidines (1 ring): Thymine, Cytosine
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Phosphodiester bonds (backbone)
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 1.2.3 Base Pairing Rules
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Aâ•T (2 hydrogen bonds)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Gâ‰¡C (3 hydrogen bonds)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Chargaff's Rules: A=T, G=C in organism
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ âš ï¸ GC-rich = More stable
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 1.2.4 Antiparallel Strands
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 5' â†’ 3' direction (phosphate â†’ hydroxyl)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Complementary strands run opposite
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Template strand: 3' â†’ 5'
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Coding strand: 5' â†’ 3' (matches mRNA)
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ 1.2.5 DNA Replication
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Semi-conservative (each new has 1 old strand)
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Key enzymes:
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Helicase: Unwinds helix
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Primase: RNA primer synthesis
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ DNA Polymerase III: Main synthesis
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ DNA Polymerase I: Primer removal
â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Ligase: Joins Okazaki fragments
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Leading strand: Continuous
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Lagging strand: Okazaki fragments
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ âš ï¸ End replication problem â†’ Telomere loss
â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€ 1.3 TRANSCRIPTION (DNA â†’ RNA)
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 1.3.1 Central Dogma
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ DNA â†’ RNA â†’ Protein
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Transcription: DNA â†’ mRNA
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Translation: mRNA â†’ Protein
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Exceptions: Reverse transcription (viruses)
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 1.3.2 RNA Types
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ mRNA (messenger): Carries genetic code
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ tRNA (transfer): Brings amino acids
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ rRNA (ribosomal): Structural in ribosomes
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ miRNA (micro): Gene regulation
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ lncRNA (long non-coding): Epigenetic control
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ snRNA (small nuclear): Splicing
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 1.3.3 Transcription Process
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ INITIATION
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ TATA box recognition (-25 bp)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Transcription factors bind
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ RNA Polymerase II recruitment
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Open complex formation
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ ELONGATION
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 5' â†’ 3' RNA synthesis
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Template strand read 3' â†’ 5'
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ ~50 nucleotides/second
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ TERMINATION
â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Poly-A signal (AAUAAA)
â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Polyadenylation & release
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ 1.3.4 mRNA Processing
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ 5' Cap: 7-methylguanosine (stability)
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ 3' Poly-A tail: 100-250 adenines
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Splicing: Intron removal
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Spliceosome (snRNPs)
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ GT-AG rule (intron boundaries)
â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Alternative splicing (multiple proteins)
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ âš ï¸ Aging: Splicing errors increase
â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€ 1.4 COMPLEMENTARY STRAND OPERATIONS
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 1.4.1 Complement Rules
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ A â†’ T, T â†’ A
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ G â†’ C, C â†’ G
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Same direction preserved
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 1.4.2 Reverse Complement (Critical!)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Step 1: Complement each base
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Step 2: Reverse the string
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Used in: PCR primers, CRISPR targets
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 1.4.3 Python Implementation
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Dictionary mapping: {'A':'T', 'T':'A', 'G':'C', 'C':'G'}
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ str.maketrans() method
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Biopython: Seq.reverse_complement()
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ 1.4.4 Applications
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ PCR primer design (3' end matches)
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ CRISPR: PAM on opposite strand
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Sequencing: Both strands for accuracy
â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€ 1.5 GC CONTENT ANALYSIS
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 1.5.1 Formula & Meaning
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ GC% = (G+C) / (A+T+G+C) Ã— 100
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Higher GC = More stable (3 H-bonds)
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Range: 20% (AT-rich) to 70% (GC-rich)
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 1.5.2 Biological Significance
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Thermophiles: High GC (heat stability)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ CpG Islands: GC-rich promoter regions
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Species identification marker
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ PCR primer design (50-60% optimal)
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ 1.5.3 ROSALIND GC Problem
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Parse multi-FASTA file
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Calculate GC% for each sequence
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Return ID with highest GC%
â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€ 1.6 MUTATIONS & VARIATIONS
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 1.6.1 Point Mutations
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Transition: Purineâ†”Purine, Pyrimidineâ†”Pyrimidine
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Transversion: Purineâ†”Pyrimidine
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Substitution types:
â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Silent: Same amino acid (codon degeneracy)
â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Missense: Different amino acid
â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Nonsense: Introduces stop codon
â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ âš ï¸ Aging: Somatic mutations accumulate
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 1.6.2 Insertion/Deletion (Indels)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Frameshift if not multiple of 3
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Usually devastating
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ In-frame: Adds/removes amino acids
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 1.6.3 Hamming Distance
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Count of differing positions
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Evolutionary distance measure
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ ROSALIND HAMM problem
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ 1.6.4 Mutation Rates
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ ~60-80 new mutations per generation
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Error rate: 1 per 10^9 bp
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ âš ï¸ Cancer: Accelerated mutations
â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€ 1.7 MOTIFS & PATTERNS
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 1.7.1 Regulatory Motifs
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ TATA Box: Promoter element (-25bp)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ CpG Islands: Methylation targets
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Kozak Sequence: Translation start context
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Polyadenylation Signal: AAUAAA
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 1.7.2 Pattern Matching
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Exact match: Find all occurrences
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Overlapping matches handling
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Regex for complex patterns
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ ROSALIND SUBS problem
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 1.7.3 Position Weight Matrices (PWM)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Frequency matrix â†’ Weight matrix
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Log-odds scoring
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Binding site prediction
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ 1.7.4 Consensus Sequences
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Most common nucleotide at each position
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Profile matrix from multiple sequences
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ ROSALIND CONS problem
â”‚
â””â”€â”€ ğŸ¯ ROSALIND PROBLEMS MODULE 1
    â”œâ”€â”€ DNA: Counting nucleotides
    â”œâ”€â”€ RNA: Transcription (Tâ†’U)
    â”œâ”€â”€ REVC: Reverse complement
    â”œâ”€â”€ GC: Highest GC content
    â”œâ”€â”€ HAMM: Hamming distance
    â”œâ”€â”€ SUBS: Finding motifs (overlapping)
    â””â”€â”€ CONS: Consensus and profile

â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

â”œâ”€â”€ 2.1 THE GENETIC CODE
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 2.1.1 Codon Structure
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 3 nucleotides = 1 codon
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 4Â³ = 64 possible codons
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 61 sense codons â†’ 20 amino acids
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ 3 stop codons: UAA, UAG, UGA
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 2.1.2 Start & Stop Codons
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ START: AUG (Methionine)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Initiator tRNA (Met-tRNAáµ¢á´¹áµ‰áµ—)
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ STOP: UAA (Ochre), UAG (Amber), UGA (Opal)
â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Release factors bind instead of tRNA
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 2.1.3 Degeneracy (Redundancy)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Multiple codons â†’ Same amino acid
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 3rd position "wobble" (flexible pairing)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Leucine: 6 codons (most)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Methionine, Tryptophan: 1 codon each
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Silent mutations possible
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 2.1.4 Amino Acid Properties
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ HYDROPHOBIC: Ala, Val, Leu, Ile, Met, Phe, Trp
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ HYDROPHILIC: Ser, Thr, Asn, Gln
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ CHARGED (+): Lys, Arg, His
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ CHARGED (-): Asp, Glu
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ SPECIAL: Cys (disulfide), Pro (rigid), Gly (flexible)
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ âš ï¸ Mutations changing properties = problematic
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ 2.1.5 Codon Table Implementation
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Dictionary: {'AUG': 'M', 'UUU': 'F', ...}
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Handle stop codons appropriately
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ ROSALIND PROT problem
â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€ 2.2 TRANSLATION MACHINERY
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 2.2.1 Ribosome Structure
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Small Subunit (40S in eukaryotes)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ mRNA binding, codon reading
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Large Subunit (60S in eukaryotes)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Peptide bond catalysis
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Complete Ribosome: 80S
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ A, P, E sites:
â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ A-site: Aminoacyl-tRNA entry
â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ P-site: Peptidyl-tRNA (growing chain)
â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ E-site: Exit (tRNA leaves)
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 2.2.2 tRNA Structure
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Cloverleaf secondary structure
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ L-shaped 3D structure
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Anticodon: Pairs with mRNA codon
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 3' CCA end: Amino acid attachment
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Aminoacyl-tRNA synthetases (20 types)
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 2.2.3 Translation Initiation
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Cap recognition (eIF4E)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 43S preinitiation complex assembly
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Scanning to first AUG
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Kozak context: GCCRCCAUGG
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ 80S ribosome formation
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 2.2.4 Translation Elongation
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Codon recognition (A-site)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Peptide bond formation (peptidyl transferase)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Translocation (EF-G)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Rate: ~6 amino acids/second
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Energy: 2 GTP per amino acid added
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ 2.2.5 Translation Termination
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Stop codon in A-site
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Release factors (eRF1, eRF3)
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Peptide release
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Ribosome recycling
â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€ 2.3 OPEN READING FRAMES (ORFs)
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 2.3.1 ORF Definition
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Sequence from START to STOP codon
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Must be in-frame (multiple of 3)
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Potential coding region
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 2.3.2 Six Reading Frames
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Forward: Frame 1, 2, 3 (offsets 0, 1, 2)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Reverse complement: Frame 4, 5, 6
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ All must be checked for genes
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 2.3.3 ORF Finding Algorithm
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ For each frame:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Scan for AUG (start)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Continue until STOP
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Record if length > threshold
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Handle nested ORFs
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ ROSALIND ORF problem
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ 2.3.4 Longest ORF = Likely Gene
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Filter by minimum length (100+ aa)
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Compare to known genes
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Gene prediction tools use this
â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€ 2.4 RNA SPLICING
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 2.4.1 Exons vs Introns
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ EXONS: Expressed (coding) regions
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ INTRONS: Intervening (non-coding) regions
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Exon-intron boundaries: GT...AG rule
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 5' splice site: GT (GU in RNA)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ 3' splice site: AG
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Average human gene: 8-10 exons
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 2.4.2 Spliceosome
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ snRNPs: U1, U2, U4, U5, U6
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Two-step transesterification
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Lariat intermediate formed
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Mature mRNA = Exons joined
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 2.4.3 Alternative Splicing
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ One gene â†’ Multiple proteins
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Types:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Exon skipping (most common)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Mutually exclusive exons
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Intron retention
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Alternative 5'/3' splice sites
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ ~95% human genes alternatively spliced
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ âš ï¸ Aging: Splicing fidelity decreases
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 2.4.4 ROSALIND SPLC Problem
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Given: DNA with intron positions
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Remove introns, join exons
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Translate to protein
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ 2.4.5 Splicing & Immortality
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Aging dysregulates splicing
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Accumulation of aberrant isoforms
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Example: SIRT1 alternative forms change with age
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Target for intervention
â”‚
â””â”€â”€ ğŸ¯ ROSALIND PROBLEMS MODULE 2
    â”œâ”€â”€ PROT: RNA to Protein translation
    â”œâ”€â”€ ORF: Finding all ORFs in sequence
    â”œâ”€â”€ SPLC: RNA splicing simulation
    â”œâ”€â”€ PRTM: Protein mass calculation
    â””â”€â”€ MRNA: Count possible RNA sources

                              ğŸ“™ MODULE 3: SEQUENCE ALIGNMENT
                                        (Month 3 â€¢ 1170+ Lines)
â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•
â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€ 3.1 ALIGNMENT FUNDAMENTALS
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 3.1.1 Why Align Sequences?
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Evolutionary relationships (homology)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Functional inference (similar = similar function)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Identify conserved regions (important sites)
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ âš ï¸ Aging genes conserved across species
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 3.1.2 Types of Alignment
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ PAIRWISE: 2 sequences
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Global: Full-length match (Needleman-Wunsch)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Local: Best matching region (Smith-Waterman)
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ MULTIPLE (MSA): 3+ sequences simultaneously
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 3.1.3 Alignment Elements
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Match: Same character (positive score)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Mismatch: Different character (negative score)
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Gap: Insertion/deletion (negative penalty)
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ 3.1.4 Alignment Scoring
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Score = Î£ matches + Î£ mismatches + Î£ gaps
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Higher score = Better alignment
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Optimal alignment = Maximum score
â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€ 3.2 SCORING SYSTEMS
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 3.2.1 Simple Scoring
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Match: +1, Mismatch: -1, Gap: -2
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ For nucleotides (simple)
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 3.2.2 Substitution Matrices (Proteins)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ PAM (Point Accepted Mutation)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ PAM1: 1% divergence
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ PAM250: Distant (~20% identity)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Based on observed mutations
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ BLOSUM (Blocks Substitution Matrix)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ BLOSUM62: Most common (62% identity threshold)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ BLOSUM80: Close sequences
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ BLOSUM45: Distant sequences
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Based on conserved protein blocks
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ When to use:
â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Close sequences: PAM40, BLOSUM80
â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Distant sequences: PAM250, BLOSUM45
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ 3.2.3 Gap Penalties
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Linear: Gap score = g Ã— length
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Affine: Gap open + Gap extend
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Open: -10 to -12
â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Extend: -0.5 to -2
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Affine is biologically realistic
â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€ 3.3 NEEDLEMAN-WUNSCH (Global)
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 3.3.1 Algorithm Concept
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Dynamic programming approach
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Build (n+1) Ã— (m+1) matrix
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Fill systematically
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Traceback for alignment
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 3.3.2 Initialization
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ F[0,0] = 0
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ F[i,0] = i Ã— gap_penalty (first column)
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ F[0,j] = j Ã— gap_penalty (first row)
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 3.3.3 Recurrence Relation
â”‚   â”‚   F[i,j] = max {
â”‚   â”‚       F[i-1,j-1] + score(Aáµ¢,Bâ±¼)   â† diagonal (match/mismatch)
â”‚   â”‚       F[i-1,j] + gap              â† up (gap in B)
â”‚   â”‚       F[i,j-1] + gap              â† left (gap in A)
â”‚   â”‚   }
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 3.3.4 Traceback
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Start at F[n,m] (bottom-right)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Follow arrows back to F[0,0]
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Reconstruct alignment
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ 3.3.5 Python Implementation
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ 2D array for scores
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ 2D array for traceback pointers
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ ROSALIND GLOB problem
â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€ 3.4 SMITH-WATERMAN (Local)
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 3.4.1 Key Differences from Global
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ No negative scores (floor at 0)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Start traceback from maximum cell
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Stop when reach 0
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Finds best local region
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 3.4.2 Modified Recurrence
â”‚   â”‚   F[i,j] = max {
â”‚   â”‚       0                            â† NEW: Reset option
â”‚   â”‚       F[i-1,j-1] + score(Aáµ¢,Bâ±¼)
â”‚   â”‚       F[i-1,j] + gap
â”‚   â”‚       F[i,j-1] + gap
â”‚   â”‚   }
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 3.4.3 Applications
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Find similar domains in unrelated proteins
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Identify conserved motifs
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Database searching foundation
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ 3.4.4 ROSALIND LOCA Problem
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Implement Smith-Waterman
â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€ 3.5 BLAST (Basic Local Alignment Search Tool)
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 3.5.1 Why BLAST Over Smith-Waterman?
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ S-W: O(nÃ—m) - Too slow for genome databases
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ BLAST: Heuristic, ~100Ã— faster
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Good enough for most purposes
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 3.5.2 BLAST Algorithm
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ SEEDING:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Break query into k-mers (words)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Find exact matches in database
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Word size: 11 (DNA), 3 (protein)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ EXTENSION:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Extend seeds in both directions
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Stop when score drops
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Creates High-Scoring Pairs (HSPs)
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ EVALUATION:
â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Calculate E-value
â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Rank hits by significance
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 3.5.3 BLAST Variants
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ BLASTN: Nucleotide vs nucleotide
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ BLASTP: Protein vs protein
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ BLASTX: Translated nucleotide vs protein
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ TBLASTN: Protein vs translated nucleotide
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ TBLASTX: Translated vs translated
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 3.5.4 Understanding E-value
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Expected number of random matches
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ E < 0.01: Significant
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ E < 1e-5: Very significant
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ E > 1: Likely random
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ 3.5.5 Using NCBI BLAST
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Web interface: blast.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Biopython: Bio.Blast.NCBIWWW
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Command-line: blast+ tools
â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€ 3.6 MULTIPLE SEQUENCE ALIGNMENT (MSA)
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 3.6.1 Why MSA?
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Compare many sequences simultaneously
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Identify highly conserved regions
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Build phylogenetic trees
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ âš ï¸ Compare TERT across species
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 3.6.2 Progressive Alignment
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Build guide tree (pairwise similarities)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Align closest sequences first
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Add sequences progressively
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ ClustalOmega, MUSCLE, MAFFT
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 3.6.3 Conservation Analysis
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Per-column conservation score
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Highly conserved = Functionally important
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Variable = Tolerant to mutation
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 3.6.4 Sequence Logos
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Visual representation of conservation
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Letter height = Information content
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Bits scale (0-2 for DNA, 0-4.32 for protein)
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ WebLogo, Logomaker
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ 3.6.5 MSA for Aging Genes
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Compare SIRT1 across mammals
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Find conserved catalytic residues
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Identify species-specific differences
â”‚
â””â”€â”€ ğŸ¯ ROSALIND PROBLEMS MODULE 3
    â”œâ”€â”€ EDIT: Edit distance calculation
    â”œâ”€â”€ GLOB: Global alignment
    â”œâ”€â”€ LOCA: Local alignment
    â””â”€â”€ GAFF: Affine gap penalties

â”œâ”€â”€ 4.1 BIOPYTHON CORE
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 4.1.1 Installation & Setup
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ pip install biopython
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ from Bio import Seq, SeqIO, Entrez
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Version check: Bio.__version__
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 4.1.2 Seq Object
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ from Bio.Seq import Seq
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ dna = Seq("ATGCGATCG")
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Methods:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ .complement() â†’ TACGCTAGC
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ .reverse_complement() â†’ CGATCGCAT
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ .transcribe() â†’ AUGCGAUCG
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ .translate() â†’ MRS... (protein)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Slicing: dna[0:3] â†’ first codon
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Immutable (like Python strings)
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 4.1.3 SeqRecord Object
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Seq + Metadata
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Attributes:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ .seq: The sequence
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ .id: Identifier
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ .name: Name
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ .description: Full description
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ .annotations: Dict of annotations
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ .features: List of SeqFeatures
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Rich representation of biological sequences
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 4.1.4 SeqIO Module
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ SeqIO.read(file, format): Single sequence
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ SeqIO.parse(file, format): Multiple (generator)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ SeqIO.write(records, file, format): Output
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Format conversion:
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ SeqIO.convert(infile, "genbank", outfile, "fasta")
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Supported: fasta, genbank, fastq, embl, ...
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ 4.1.5 Practical Examples
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Count nucleotides in FASTA
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Translate all ORFs
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Extract features from GenBank

â”œâ”€â”€ 4.2 NCBI ACCESS (Entrez)
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 4.2.1 Setup
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ from Bio import Entrez
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Entrez.email = "your@email.com" (REQUIRED!)
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Rate limit: 3 requests/second
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 4.2.2 Entrez.esearch()
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Search database for IDs
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ handle = Entrez.esearch(db="nucleotide", term="TERT[Gene] AND human")
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ record = Entrez.read(handle)
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ record["IdList"] â†’ List of GI numbers
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 4.2.3 Entrez.efetch()
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Download by ID
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ handle = Entrez.efetch(db="nucleotide", id="NM_198253", 
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚                         rettype="fasta", retmode="text")
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ record = SeqIO.read(handle, "fasta")
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 4.2.4 Entrez.einfo()
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Database information
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Available fields, record counts
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 4.2.5 Key Databases
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ nucleotide: DNA/RNA sequences (GenBank)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ protein: Protein sequences
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ gene: Gene information
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ pubmed: Literature
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ geo: Expression data
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ 4.2.6 Batch Downloads
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Loop with time.sleep(0.34) for rate limit
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Use id as comma-separated list for batch
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Error handling for network issues
â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€ 4.3 BIOLOGICAL DATABASES
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 4.3.1 Sequence Databases
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ NCBI GenBank
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ User-submitted sequences
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Accessions: NC_, NM_, NR_, NP_
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Comprehensive but redundant
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ RefSeq
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ NCBI-curated, non-redundant
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Higher quality annotations
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Prefixes indicate type
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ UniProt
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Swiss-Prot: Curated (reviewed)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ TrEMBL: Automatic (unreviewed)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Rich functional annotations
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Ensembl
â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Genome browser & annotations
â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Gene predictions
â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Comparative genomics
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 4.3.2 Expression Databases
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ GEO (Gene Expression Omnibus)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Microarray & RNA-seq data
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ GSE (series), GSM (samples)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ GEOquery for R, GEOparse for Python
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ ArrayExpress (EMBL-EBI)
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ GTEx (Genotype-Tissue Expression)
â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Normal tissue expression atlas
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 4.3.3 Aging-Specific Databases âš ï¸
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ HAGR (Human Ageing Genomic Resources)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ GenAge: Aging-related genes
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ AnAge: Longevity data by species
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ LongevityMap: Variants affecting lifespan
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ CellAge: Senescence genes
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ AgingAtlas
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ SeneQuest (senescence database)
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ DrugAge (anti-aging drugs)

â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ ClinVar: Clinical variant significance
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ gnomAD: Population variant frequencies
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ dbSNP: SNP catalog
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ COSMIC: Cancer mutations

â”œâ”€â”€ 4.4 FILE FORMATS
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 4.4.1 Sequence Formats
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ FASTA
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ >header\nSEQUENCE
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Simple, universal
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ No quality scores
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ FASTQ
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ @header\nSEQUENCE\n+\nQUALITY
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Phred quality scores (ASCII)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Raw sequencing output
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ GenBank (.gb, .gbk)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Rich annotations
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ LOCUS, FEATURES, ORIGIN sections
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Standard for annotated sequences
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ EMBL
â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ European equivalent to GenBank
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 4.4.2 Alignment/Mapping Formats
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ SAM/BAM
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Sequence Alignment/Map
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ SAM = text, BAM = binary (compressed)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Read alignments to reference
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ pysam library for Python
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ VCF (Variant Call Format)
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ CHROM, POS, REF, ALT, QUAL, FILTER, INFO
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Genotype data
â”‚   â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ PyVCF, cyvcf2 for parsing
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ BED
â”‚   â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Genomic regions (chrom, start, end)
â”‚   â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Simple, tab-delimited
â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ 4.4.3 Annotation Formats
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ GFF/GTF
â”‚       â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Gene features, coordinates
â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ 9-column format
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ WIG/BigWig
â”‚       â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Continuous signal data
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ BED variants
â”‚           â””â”€â”€ narrowPeak, broadPeak (ChIP-seq)
â”‚

                                        (Month 5 â€¢ 1115+ Lines)
â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•
â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€ 5.1 VARIANT TYPES
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 5.1.1 SNPs (Single Nucleotide Polymorphisms)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Single base change (Aâ†’G, Câ†’T, etc.)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Most common variation (~4-5M per genome)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Transitions vs Transversions
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ dbSNP: rs#### identifiers
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 5.1.2 Indels
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Insertions: Extra nucleotides
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Deletions: Missing nucleotides
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Frameshift if not 3x
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 5.1.3 Structural Variants (SVs)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ CNVs: Copy Number Variations (>1kb)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Inversions: Flipped segments
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Translocations: Moved segments
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Large deletions/duplications
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ 5.1.4 âš ï¸ Longevity Variants
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ APOE: rs429358, rs7412 (E2/E3/E4)
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ FOXO3: rs2802292 (protective G allele)
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ TERT: rs2736100 (telomere length)
â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€ 5.2 VCF FORMAT DEEP DIVE
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 5.2.1 File Structure
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Meta-lines: ##INFO, ##FORMAT
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Header: #CHROM POS ID REF ALT...
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Data lines: Actual variants
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 5.2.2 Key Columns
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ CHROM: Chromosome
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ POS: Position (1-based)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ ID: rs number or .
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ REF/ALT: Reference/Alternate alleles
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ QUAL: Phred quality score
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ FILTER: PASS or fail reasons
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ INFO: Annotations (AF, DP, etc.)
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 5.2.3 Genotype Fields

â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ PyVCF: import vcf

â”œâ”€â”€ 5.3 GWAS (Genome-Wide Association)
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 5.3.1 Study Design
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Case-control: Disease vs healthy
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Quantitative traits: Continuous measures
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Sample sizes: 10,000+ for power
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 5.3.2 Statistics
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Odds Ratio (OR): Effect size
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ P-value: Significance
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Multiple testing: Bonferroni
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Genome-wide: p < 5Ã—10â»â¸
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 5.3.3 Manhattan Plots
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ X: Chromosome position
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Y: -log10(p-value)
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Peaks = Significant loci

â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ APOE: Strongest hit (Alzheimer's risk)

                              ğŸ”µ MODULE 8: CRISPR-Cas9 SYSTEM
                                        (Month 9 â€¢ 800+ Lines)
â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•
â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€ 8.1 CRISPR FUNDAMENTALS
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 8.1.1 Discovery & History
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Bacterial immune system
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 2012: Doudna & Charpentier
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ 2020 Nobel Prize
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 8.1.2 Cas9 Structure
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ RuvC domain: Cuts non-target strand
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ HNH domain: Cuts target strand
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ PAM recognition domain
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Size: ~160 kDa
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 8.1.3 Guide RNA (sgRNA)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 20bp spacer: Target complementary
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Scaffold: Cas9 binding
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Synthetic fusion (crRNA + tracrRNA)
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ 8.1.4 PAM Requirement
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ SpCas9: NGG (3' of target)
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ SaCas9: NNGRRT
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Cpf1/Cas12a: TTTN
â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€ 8.2 DNA REPAIR PATHWAYS
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 8.2.1 NHEJ (Knockout)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Error-prone repair
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Creates indels â†’ Frameshift
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Gene knockout
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Active throughout cell cycle
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 8.2.2 HDR (Knock-in)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ High-fidelity with template
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Precise editing possible
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Only in S/G2 phase
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Lower efficiency than NHEJ
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ 8.2.3 Template Design
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ ssODN: Small edits (<50bp)
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ dsDNA: Large insertions
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Homology arms: 30-800bp
â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€ 8.3 gRNA DESIGN
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 8.3.1 Design Rules
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 20bp spacer before NGG
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ GC content: 40-70%
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Avoid poly-T (transcription terminator)
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Check seed region (12bp proximal to PAM)
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 8.3.2 Off-Target Prediction
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Mismatches in seed = Fewer off-targets
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ PAM-distal more tolerated
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Algorithms: CFD score, MIT score
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Genome-wide off-target search
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ 8.3.3 Design Tools
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ CRISPOR: crispor.tefor.net
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Benchling: Design & tracking
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ CHOPCHOP, E-CRISP
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Python: crispy, gRNA design scripts
â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€ 8.4 BASE EDITING
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 8.4.1 CBE (Cytosine Base Editor)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ dCas9/nCas9 + APOBEC deaminase
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Câ€¢G â†’ Tâ€¢A conversion
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ No double-strand break
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Editing window: 4-8bp
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 8.4.2 ABE (Adenine Base Editor)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ dCas9/nCas9 + evolved TadA
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Aâ€¢T â†’ Gâ€¢C conversion
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Editing window: 4-7bp
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ 8.4.3 Advantages
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ ~60% pathogenic SNPs correctable
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ No NHEJ/HDR needed
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Fewer indels
â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€ 8.5 PRIME EDITING
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 8.5.1 Mechanism
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Cas9 nickase + Reverse Transcriptase
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ pegRNA: spacer + PBS + RT template
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ "Search and replace" for genome
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ All 12 point mutations + small indels
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 8.5.2 pegRNA Design
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ PBS: Primer Binding Site (13bp)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ RT template: Contains desired edit
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Optimization required
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ 8.5.3 Applications
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Precise corrections
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Tag insertions
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Disease modeling
â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€ 8.6 CRISPRa/CRISPRi (Regulation)
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 8.6.1 CRISPRa (Activation) âš ï¸
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ dCas9 + Activators (VP64, VPR, SAM)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Target promoter region
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ No DNA cutting
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ âš ï¸ ACTIVATE TERT for telomere extension!
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ 8.6.2 CRISPRi (Interference)
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ dCas9 + KRAB repressor
â”‚   â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Block transcription
â”‚   â”‚   â””â”€â”€ âš ï¸ SILENCE CDKN2A (p16) to reduce senescence
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ 8.6.3 Reversibility
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Unlike knockout: Reversible
â”‚       â”œâ”€â”€ Tunable expression
â”‚       â””â”€â”€ Safer for therapeutics
â”‚
â””â”€â”€ ğŸ¯ PROJECT: LONGEVITY GENE PANEL DESIGN
    â”œâ”€â”€ Design gRNAs for: TERT, SIRT1, FOXO3, CDKN2A
    â”œâ”€â”€ Create CRISPRa constructs for activation
    â”œâ”€â”€ Design CRISPRi for senescence genes
    â””â”€â”€ Off-target analysis

â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•
